**Phase 111 — Complete.** All 239 test modules green. Sovereign Morris Counter (Morris, 1978 — *Counting large numbers of events in small registers*) — the original **approximate counting** algorithm. Counting to `n` exactly needs `⌈log₂ n⌉` bits; the Morris counter stores only a small **exponent register** `c` and reaches an estimate of `n` in `≈ log₂ log₂ n` bits by incrementing `c` only *probabilistically*. For the generalised base `a > 1` (Flajolet 1985): on each event `c ← c + 1` with probability `a^(−c)`, and the estimate is `n̂ = (a^c − 1)/(a − 1)`. The estimate is **unbiased** — `E[n̂] = n` for all `n` — which follows by induction (`E[a^c]` rises by exactly `a − 1` per event, so `E[a^c] = 1 + n·(a − 1)`); the classic **base-2** case is the familiar `increment with prob 2^(−c)`, `n̂ = 2^c − 1`. The base trades memory for accuracy (variance `≈ n·(n − 1)·(a − 1)/2`): a base near 1 is very accurate but the register grows almost like an exact counter, while a larger base keeps the register tiny at higher variance (measured: base-2 register `c = 16` for `n = 100 000`; mean estimate over 400 seeds within ~5 % of `n`; mean |rel error| 0.17 at base 1.1 vs 0.47 at base 2.0). This is a **new feature-class** — *approximate counting* — distinct from the cardinality sketches (HyperLogLog/P74, Theta/P93, which count *distinct* items) and the frequency sketches (Count-Min/P76, Count-Sketch/P94, per-key counts): the Morris counter estimates a single running **event total**. The compact state is the single integer `register`; an exact `increments` tally is kept only so `stats`/`relative_error` can report observed accuracy (a memory-constrained deployment would omit it). The probabilistic coin is a `random.Random(seed)`, so a fixed seed + increment sequence reproduce the counter exactly. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/morris_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 111A: `pradyos/core/morris_counter.py` — `MorrisCounterError(detail)`; `MorrisCounter(base=2.0, seed=0)` with `increment(times=1)` (each event bumps `c` with prob `base^(−c)`; returns the new register; `MorrisCounterError` on `times ∉ ℤ⁺`), `estimate()` (`(base^c − 1)/(base − 1)`), `relative_error()` (`|estimate − increments|/increments`, 0 when empty), `reset(base=None, seed=None)` (re-seeds the RNG), and `register` (c) / `increments` (exact n) / `base` / `seed` properties, plus `stats()` (register / estimate / increments / base / relative_error / seed). Invalid `base` (∉ (1, ∞)) or `seed` raise `MorrisCounterError` (bools rejected; `int` base coerced to `float`).
- ✅ 111B: `pradyos/web/morris_web.py` — `register_morris_routes(app, morris_counter=None)` (defaults to a fresh `MorrisCounter`) mounts 4 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/morris/increment` (body `{times?}`, default 1; **422** on `times ∉ ℤ⁺`), `GET /api/v1/morris/estimate` (`{estimate, register}`), `GET /api/v1/morris/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/morris/reset` (body `{base?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 111C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase111.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `morris_counter` param, and a single `register_morris_routes(app, morris_counter)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 111D: `tests/test_morris_counter.py` (41) + `tests/test_morris_web.py` (19) — **unbiasedness** (mean estimate over 400 seeds within 10 % of `n` at base 2, within 8 % at base 1.5); **log-log register** (`c < 30` for `n = 100 000`); **base-2 formula** (`estimate == 2^c − 1`) + **general-base formula**; **smaller base lowers variance** (mean |rel error| base 1.1 < base 2.0); **determinism** (same seed + sequence → identical register/estimate; `increment(n)` ≡ `n×increment(1)`; different seed diverges; reset re-seeds); **monotonic** register; validation (`base ≤ 1`, non-number, bools, `times ∈ {0, −5, 2.5, "x"}`) + `MorrisCounterError.detail`; properties; relative_error (mean ≈ 0.25 at base 1.2) / stats / reset; 10-thread concurrent increments (exact tally under the lock); all 4 endpoints over HTTP incl. `DELETE`-with-body reset + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `stablebloom`).
- ✅ 111E: `scripts/prove.py` — 239 test modules registered (Phase 111 appends `test_morris_counter.py` + `test_morris_web.py`).
- ✅ 111F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 112 planned.

**Phase 112 — Complete.** All 241 test modules green. Sovereign Linear Counting (Whang, Vander-Zanden & Taylor, 1990 — *A linear-time probabilistic counting algorithm for database applications*) — a **cardinality** (distinct-count) estimator markedly more accurate than HyperLogLog at *small-to-moderate* cardinalities, for more space. The structure is one **bitmap** of `m` bits; each item is hashed to one position `h(x) mod m` and that bit is set, so duplicates collapse and the bitmap depends only on the *distinct* items. After the stream, the count is estimated from the **fraction of still-zero bits** `V = zero_bits/m`: `n̂ = −m·ln(V)`. The derivation is the balls-in-bins empty-bin expectation — a bit is zero iff no distinct item hashed to it, so `E[zero_bits] = m·(1 − 1/m)^n ≈ m·e^(−n/m)`, giving `E[V] ≈ e^(−n/m)` and `n ≈ −m·ln(V)` (measured: sub-1 % relative error to load ~0.8; zero-bit count within 0.1 % of `m·e^(−n/m)`). Once **every** bit is set the bitmap is *saturated*, `V = 0`, and the estimate is undefined — `estimate()` raises `LinearCounterError`. This is a *different* cardinality algorithm from HyperLogLog (P74 — maximum leading-zero registers) and the Theta sketch (P93 — KMV / k-minimum-values): bitmap-and-empty-bins rather than order statistics, matching the one-algorithm-per-method pattern. Hashing is a single seeded BLAKE2b digest; a running set-bit count keeps `estimate` O(1). Pure stdlib (`hashlib`); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/linear_counter_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 112A: `pradyos/core/linear_counter.py` — `LinearCounterError(detail)`; `LinearCounter(num_bits=65536, seed=0)` with `add(item)` (idempotent bit-set; distinct-count semantics), `add_many(items)` (`LinearCounterError` on a non-iterable), `estimate()` (`−m·ln(V)`; **raises when saturated**), `reset(num_bits=None, seed=None)`, `load_factor()`, `__len__` (bits set), and `num_bits` (m) / `bits_set` / `seed` / `saturated` properties, plus `stats()` (num_bits / bits_set / zero_bits / load_factor / estimate (None if saturated) / seed). Invalid `num_bits` (∉ ℤ⁺) or `seed` raise `LinearCounterError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 112B: `pradyos/web/linear_counter_web.py` — `register_linearcounting_routes(app, linear_counter=None)` (defaults to a fresh `LinearCounter`) mounts 4 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/linearcounting/add` (body `{element}`; 422 on missing / non-dict), `GET /api/v1/linearcounting/estimate` (`{estimate, bits_set}`; **400 when saturated** — a state error), `GET /api/v1/linearcounting/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/linearcounting/reset` (body `{num_bits?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 112C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase112.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `linear_counter` param, and a single `register_linearcounting_routes(app, linear_counter)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 112D: `tests/test_linear_counter.py` (35) + `tests/test_linearcounting_web.py` (17) — **accuracy** (rel error `< 0.03` at loads 0.07 / 0.26 / 0.53 / 0.76); **idempotent distinct-count** (1000× the same item → estimate ≈ 1; 3000 distinct from 15 000 adds → ≈ 3000); **zero-bit law** (measured zeros within 2 % of `m·e^(−n/m)`); **larger `m` lowers error**; **saturation** (`saturated` flag + `estimate()` raises + `stats.estimate is None`); **determinism** (same seed → identical bitmap/estimate; different seed diverges the bitmap but the estimate stays within 5 %); config validation + `add_many` non-iterable + `LinearCounterError.detail`; properties / load_factor / stats; reset clears + reconfigures + re-add; 10-thread concurrent adds (estimate within 5 % of 5000 distinct); all 4 endpoints over HTTP incl. the saturated **400**, `DELETE`-with-body reset + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `morris`).

**Phase 113 — Complete.** All 243 test modules green. Sovereign Treap (Seidel & Aragon, 1996 — *Randomized search trees*) — a **randomized balanced binary search tree**. Each node is simultaneously BST-ordered by `key` and max-heap-ordered by a **random priority**; the heap constraint forces a unique tree shape — the one a plain BST would take if keys were inserted in decreasing-priority order — and since the priorities are random, that order is a uniformly random permutation, so the tree behaves like a BST built from random insertions: **expected height `≈ 2·ln n`** and `search` / `insert` / `delete` / `rank` / `select` all `O(log n)` *expected*, with no balance-factor or colour bookkeeping. `insert` does a BST insert then rotates the new node up while its priority exceeds its parent's; `delete` removes a node by **merging its two subtrees** (higher-priority child becomes the local root, recursively). Every node stores its **subtree size**, making the order-statistics `rank(key)` (keys strictly smaller) and `select(i)` (the `i`-th smallest key) run in `O(log n)`. Measured: height 32 for `n = 5000` random keys (`2·ln n ≈ 17`), and — the key property — **sorted inserts stay balanced** (height 28, where a plain BST would be 5000) because random priorities defeat adversarial order. This is a *different* probabilistic ordered structure from the Skip List (P78, randomized tower levels over a linked list) — random priorities + rotations over a tree — matching the one-algorithm-per-method pattern. Priorities come from a seeded `random.Random` so a fixed seed + insertion sequence reproduce the tree exactly. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/treap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 113A: `pradyos/core/treap.py` — `TreapError(detail)`; `Treap(seed=0)` with `insert(key, value=None)` (BST insert + rotate-up; updates value in place on a duplicate, no growth), `delete(key)` → bool (subtree merge), `contains(key)` / `__contains__`, `search(key)` (raises if absent) / `get(key, default=None)`, `rank(key)`, `select(index)` (raises out of range), `min_key()` / `max_key()` (raise when empty), `keys()` (in-order, iterative), `height()`, `reset(seed=None)` (re-seeds priorities), `__len__`, and `seed` property, plus `stats()` (size / height / min / max / seed). Invalid `seed` raises `TreapError` (bools rejected); every node keeps a maintained `size`.
- ✅ 113B: `pradyos/web/treap_web.py` — `register_treap_routes(app, treap=None)` (defaults to a fresh `Treap`) mounts 7 (all-static) routes with **numeric keys** (so the order statistics have a total order): `POST /api/v1/treap/insert` (body `{key, value?}`; 422 on missing / non-numeric key), `DELETE /api/v1/treap/delete` (body `{key}`; 422 on bad key), `GET /api/v1/treap/search` (`?key=`), `GET /api/v1/treap/rank` (`?key=`), `GET /api/v1/treap/select` (`?index=` `Query(ge=0)`; **400 when out of range** — a state error), `GET /api/v1/treap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/treap/reset` (body `{seed?}`).

**Phase 114 — Complete.** All 245 test modules green. Sovereign Bloomier Filter (Chazelle, Kilian, Rubinfeld & Tal, 2004 — *The Bloomier filter: an efficient data structure for static support lookup tables*) — the **associative** generalisation of a Bloom filter: instead of *is `x` in the set?* it answers *what value is associated with `x`?* for a **static** key→value map. Construction is the same **XOR-peeling** the platform's XOR (P100) and Binary-Fuse (P108) filters use, generalised from storing a fingerprint to storing a *payload*: each key hashes (one seeded mix sliced into three segment-local indices) to three table cells, the cells are assigned by peeling the 3-XOR hypergraph and back-substituting in reverse peel order so that for every key `array[h0] ^ array[h1] ^ array[h2] == payload`, where `payload = (fingerprint << value_bits) | value_index`. A lookup XORs the three cells, splits out the fingerprint and value index, and — *only if the fingerprint matches the key's own* — returns `value_table[value_index]`. So **members are answered exactly** (measured: 0 wrong over 5000 keys) while a **non-member is reported not-found with probability `1 − 2^(−fingerprint_bits)`** (measured 0.0024 ≈ 2⁻⁸; ~0 at 16 bits — a fingerprint collision is the only false-positive path). Values are stored verbatim in a positional value table (no hashing of values, so *unhashable* values like lists/dicts work); keys fold to a stable 64-bit BLAKE2b of `repr(key)`; peeling stalls trigger a deterministic seed retry. This is a **new capability** — value *retrieval*, not just membership (Bloom/P72, Counting/P107) or counts — and a different construction target from the membership-only XOR/Fuse filters. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.RLock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/bloomier_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 114A: `pradyos/core/bloomier.py` — `BloomierError(detail)`; `BloomierFilter(fingerprint_bits=8, seed=0)` with `build(mapping)` (static; sorts by folded key, `value_bits = (n−1).bit_length()`, `BloomierError` on a key hash-collision or peeling cycle after the seed retries), `get(key, default=None)` (exact for members; `default` otherwise; raises before build), `contains(key)` / `__contains__`, `reset(seed=None)` (back to unbuilt), `__len__`, and `seed` / `built` / `fingerprint_bits` / `num_cells` properties, plus `stats()` (built / num_keys / num_cells / fingerprint_bits / value_bits / bits_per_key / seed). Invalid `fingerprint_bits` (∉ 1..32) / `seed` raise `BloomierError` (bools rejected); segments sized at `⌈1.23·n/3⌉ + 4` like the Binary-Fuse filter.
- ✅ 114B: `pradyos/web/bloomier_web.py` — `register_bloomier_routes(app, bloomier=None)` (defaults to a fresh unbuilt filter) mounts 4 (all-static) routes — **no insert (the map is static)**: `POST /api/v1/bloomier/build` (body `{mapping: {...}}`; 422 on missing / non-object mapping, **400** on cycle / duplicate), `GET /api/v1/bloomier/get` (`?key=`; `{key, found, value}`; **400 before build**), `GET /api/v1/bloomier/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/bloomier/reset` (body `{seed?}`; 422 on bad seed).
- ✅ 114C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase114.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `bloomier` param, and a single `register_bloomier_routes(app, bloomier)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 114D: `tests/test_bloomier.py` (38) + `tests/test_bloomier_web.py` (20) — **exact value for every member** (small & 3000-key); **non-member FP** ≤ 0.02 over 10 000 probes (≈ 2⁻⁸) + **wider fingerprint** (16-bit ≤ 0.001); **arbitrary / unhashable values** (lists, dicts, None, floats) verbatim; **numeric keys**; **determinism** (same seed → identical array & value table) + **order-independence** (shuffled dict → identical array); **immutability** (rebuild replaces); **build across sizes** `n = 1..300` (incl. the `n=1`, `value_bits=0` edge); **empty build**; `contains` (members True, non-members ≈ FP); not-built / reset (`get`/`contains` raise before build; reset → unbuilt + rebuildable); config validation (`fingerprint_bits ∈ {0,64,8.5,bool}`, bad seed, non-mapping, **duplicate keys via a fake `.items()`**) + `BloomierError.detail`; properties / stats (built & unbuilt, `value_bits == (n−1).bit_length()`); 10-thread concurrent `get` (all values exact); all 4 endpoints over HTTP incl. the build/`get` **400**s, `DELETE`-with-body reset + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `treap`).

**Phase 115 — Complete.** All 247 test modules green. Sovereign MinHash LSH (Indyk & Motwani 1998; Broder 1997 — *locality-sensitive hashing* over MinHash signatures) — a **similarity-search index** for fast approximate near-duplicate / nearest-neighbour retrieval over sets. The platform already *estimates* set similarity (MinHash/P88, SimHash/P89); LSH turns that into an **index**. Each item's token set is reduced to a `k = bands·rows` MinHash signature via universal hashing `h_i(t) = (a_i·base(t) + b_i) mod (2⁶¹−1)`, `signature[i] = min_t h_i(t)` (two sets agree on a position with probability equal to their Jaccard similarity `s`). The signature is split into `bands` bands of `rows` rows; an item is bucketed per band by that band's whole `rows`-tuple, so two items collide in a band iff their signatures agree on every row of it (`s^rows`) and share **at least one** band with probability `1 − (1 − s^rows)^bands` — the classic LSH **S-curve** with threshold `≈ (1/bands)^(1/rows)`. `query(set)` gathers the candidates sharing any band bucket and refines them by the signature-agreement estimate, returning those at/above a similarity threshold (sorted by descending similarity). Measured: self-query similarity 1.0, Jaccard estimates within ~0.05–0.1 of truth, **recall 1.0** on ~0.8-Jaccard near-duplicates over 200 docs, disjoint sets excluded. This is a *new capability* — similarity **search / indexing**, not just pairwise estimation. Fully deterministic given the seed (universal-hash coefficients seeded; results sorted by similarity then stringified id, so output never depends on set iteration order). Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/minhash_lsh_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 115A: `pradyos/core/minhash_lsh.py` — `MinHashLSHError(detail)`; `MinHashLSH(bands=16, rows=4, seed=0)` with `insert(item_id, tokens)` (re-insert replaces), `query(tokens, threshold=0.0)` → `[(id, similarity), ...]` desc, `similarity(a, b)` (signature-agreement Jaccard estimate), `remove(item_id)` → bool, `contains(item_id)` / `__contains__`, `reset(bands=None, rows=None, seed=None)`, `threshold_estimate()` (`(1/bands)^(1/rows)`), `__len__`, and `bands` / `rows` / `num_perm` (k) / `seed` properties, plus `stats()` (num_items / bands / rows / num_perm / threshold_estimate / seed). Invalid `bands` / `rows` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `seed` / `threshold` (∉ [0,1]) raise `MinHashLSHError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 115B: `pradyos/web/minhash_lsh_web.py` — `register_minhashlsh_routes(app, minhash_lsh=None)` (defaults to a fresh index) mounts 5 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/minhashlsh/insert` (body `{id, tokens[]}`; 422 on missing id / non-list tokens), `POST /api/v1/minhashlsh/query` (body `{tokens[], threshold?}`; 422 on non-list tokens / bad threshold), `DELETE /api/v1/minhashlsh/remove` (body `{id}`), `GET /api/v1/minhashlsh/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/minhashlsh/reset` (body `{bands?, rows?, seed?}`).
- ✅ 115C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase115.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `minhash_lsh` param, and a single `register_minhashlsh_routes(app, minhash_lsh)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 115D: `tests/test_minhash_lsh.py` (35) + `tests/test_minhashlsh_web.py` (21) — **self-query** finds self at sim≈1; **similarity estimate** within 0.1 of true Jaccard (identical→1, disjoint→~0); **retrieval** (near-duplicate found, disjoint excluded, threshold filters by estimate, **recall ≥ 0.9** over 200 near-dups, results sorted desc, multiple overlapping windows all retrieved); **determinism** (same seed → identical query results & signatures); **remove / re-insert** (replaces signature, removed not in query); empty token set + string tokens; validation (`bands`/`rows`/`seed`/`threshold ∉ [0,1]`, bools) + `MinHashLSHError.detail`; properties / `threshold_estimate` / stats; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. `DELETE`-with-body remove/reset + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `bloomier`).

**Phase 116 — Complete.** All 249 test modules green. Sovereign TinyLFU (Einziger, Friedman & Manes, 2017 — *TinyLFU: a highly efficient cache admission policy*) — a **frequency sketch with aging**, the recency-aware estimator behind modern cache-admission policies (e.g. Caffeine's W-TinyLFU). A plain Count-Min (P76) never forgets, so on a long stream every counter saturates and current popularity is indistinguishable from stale popularity. TinyLFU adds the two ingredients a cache needs: a **doorkeeper** — a small Bloom filter that absorbs *one-hit wonders* (a key's first access only sets a doorkeeper bit; the larger Count-Min array is touched only from the second access on, and the estimate adds the bit back: `estimate(x) = countmin(x) + (1 if x in doorkeeper)`); and a **reset / aging** rule — a running access counter bumps on every access, and once it reaches the sample size `W` the sketch *ages*: every counter is **halved** (`c >>= 1`) and the doorkeeper cleared, so the estimate tracks a *sliding* frequency that decays. The headline op `admit(candidate, victim)` → `estimate(candidate) > estimate(victim)` is the frequency-based eviction decision. Measured: exact frequency below the one-byte saturation (caps at 256), one-sided error (`estimate ≥ true`), singletons leave the Count-Min untouched, and a heavy key's estimate **decays 60 → 3** after the sketch is aged by flooding. This is a *new feature-class* — **windowed / aging frequency for admission** — distinct from the platform's plain frequency sketches (Count-Min/P76, Count-Sketch/P94) and heavy-hitter trackers (Space-Saving/P87, Misra-Gries/P99, HeavyKeeper/P102), none of which age. Counters are one byte each (saturating) in a flat `bytearray`; hashing is double-hashing from one seeded BLAKE2b digest. Fully deterministic given the seed. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/tiny_lfu_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 116A: `pradyos/core/tiny_lfu.py` — `TinyLFUError(detail)`; `TinyLFU(sample_size=1000, width=None, depth=4, seed=0)` (`width` defaults to `sample_size`) with `add(key)` (doorkeeper on first sight, Count-Min after; ages at `sample_size`), `estimate(key)` (Count-Min min + doorkeeper bit), `admit(candidate, victim)` → bool, `reset(sample_size=None, width=None, depth=None, seed=None)`, and `sample_size` / `width` / `depth` / `seed` / `total` / `resets` properties, plus `stats()` (sample_size / width / depth / doorkeeper_bits / total / accesses_since_reset / resets / seed). The doorkeeper is a Bloom sized for ~1 % FP at the sample size. Invalid `sample_size` / `width` / `depth` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `seed` raise `TinyLFUError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 116B: `pradyos/web/tiny_lfu_web.py` — `register_tinylfu_routes(app, tiny_lfu=None)` (defaults to a fresh sketch) mounts 5 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/tinylfu/add` (body `{key}`; 422 on missing), `GET /api/v1/tinylfu/estimate` (`?key=`), `POST /api/v1/tinylfu/admit` (body `{candidate, victim}`; 422 on missing), `GET /api/v1/tinylfu/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/tinylfu/reset` (body `{sample_size?, width?, depth?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).

Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 116D: `tests/test_tiny_lfu.py` (33) + `tests/test_tinylfu_web.py` (19) — **frequency** (isolated exact below saturation; byte-counter caps at 256; **one-sided** `estimate ≥ true` over 10 000 accesses; never-added → 0); **doorkeeper** (one-hit estimate 1, Count-Min stays 0; second access touches it); **admission** (hot > cold, `admit` both directions); **aging** (heavy key decays after a flood; `resets` tracks `total // sample_size`; counters halved on reset; `accesses_since_reset`); **determinism** (same seed + sequence → identical counters & estimates); config validation (`sample_size`/`width`/`depth`/`seed`, bools) + width default + `TinyLFUError.detail`; properties / stats; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent adds; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. aging over HTTP + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `minhashlsh`).

**Phase 117 — Complete.** All 251 test modules green. Sovereign HyperMinHash (Yu & Weber, 2017 — *MinHash in LogLog space*) — a single compact sketch that estimates **both cardinality and Jaccard similarity** (hence union/intersection sizes), where the platform otherwise keeps those separate (HyperLogLog/P74 & Theta/P93 for cardinality; MinHash/P88 for similarity). Each element hashes to 64 bits: the top `p` bits choose one of `m = 2^p` **buckets**, and the remaining `w = 64 − p` bits give a HyperLogLog **rank** (`leading_zeros + 1`) and an `r`-bit **mantissa** (their low `r` bits). Since the smallest remaining hash has the most leading zeros, "keep the bucket minimum" and "keep the max HLL rank" coincide; each bucket stores the `(rank, mantissa)` of its extremal element (max rank, ties by min mantissa — order-independent and **mergeable** by bucketwise max-rank/min-mantissa). **Cardinality** uses the ranks via the standard HyperLogLog estimator `α_m·m²/Σ2^(−rank)` with the small-range linear-counting correction (measured **within ~2–4 %** of true across 1k–50k). **Jaccard** counts buckets agreeing on both rank and mantissa; the raw agreement `J + (1−J)·C` is corrected by the expected random-collision rate `C = (Σ_k P_A(k)·P_B(k))·2^(−r)` from the two rank distributions, giving `Ĵ = (agree − C)/(1 − C)` (measured **within ~0.06 absolute** across overlap levels — the residual is a known bias of the compact `(rank, mantissa)` representation; union within ~6 %, intersection within ~20 % as the product compounds). Mergeable, so distributed partitions combine bucketwise. This is a *new capability* — a **joint cardinality + similarity** sketch. Fully deterministic given the seed. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/hyper_minhash_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 117A: `pradyos/core/hyper_minhash.py` — `HyperMinHashError(detail)`; `HyperMinHash(p=8, r=8, seed=0)` (`m = 2^p`; `r`-bit mantissa) with `add(element)` / `add_many(iter)`, `cardinality()` (HLL + linear-counting), `jaccard(other)` (collision-corrected), `merge(other)` → union sketch, `union_cardinality(other)`, `intersection_cardinality(other)` (Jaccard × union), `reset(p=None, r=None, seed=None)`, and `p` / `r` / `num_buckets` / `seed` properties, plus `stats()` (p / r / num_buckets / filled / cardinality / seed). Ranks + mantissas are one byte each (`bytearray`). Invalid `p` (∉ 4..20) / `r` (∉ 1..8) / `seed`, or an incompatible (`p`/`r`/`seed`-mismatched) `other`, raise `HyperMinHashError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 117B: `pradyos/web/hyper_minhash_web.py` — `register_hyperminhash_routes(app, hyper_minhash=None)` (defaults to a fresh sketch) mounts 5 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/hyperminhash/add` (body `{element}`; 422 on missing), `GET /api/v1/hyperminhash/cardinality`, `POST /api/v1/hyperminhash/compare` (body `{tokens[]}`; builds a compatible temp sketch → `{jaccard, union, intersection}`; 422 on non-list tokens), `GET /api/v1/hyperminhash/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/hyperminhash/reset` (body `{p?, r?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 117C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase117.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `hyper_minhash` param, and a single `register_hyperminhash_routes(app, hyper_minhash)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 117D: `tests/test_hyper_minhash.py` (33) + `tests/test_hyperminhash_web.py` (18) — **cardinality** (within 5 % at 1k/10k; ignores duplicates; `add_many`); **Jaccard** (self = 1, disjoint ≈ 0, within 0.10 across overlaps, symmetric); **union** (within 6 %) / **intersection** (within 20 %); **merge** (bucketwise = the directly-built union sketch); **determinism** (same seed → identical ranks/mantissas/cardinality; different seed diverges); **compatibility** (mismatched `p`/`seed` or non-sketch `other` raise) + config validation (`p ∈ {3,21}`, `r ∈ {0,9}`, bools) + `add_many` non-iterable + `HyperMinHashError.detail`; properties / stats; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent adds; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. `compare` (self/partial/disjoint) + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `tinylfu`).
- ✅ 117E: `scripts/prove.py` — 251 test modules registered (Phase 117 appends `test_hyper_minhash.py` + `test_hyperminhash_web.py`).

**Phase 118 — Complete.** All 253 test modules green. Sovereign Scalable Bloom Filter (Almeida, Baquero, Preguiça & Hutchison, 2007 — *Scalable Bloom Filters*) — a Bloom variant for **sets of unknown, growing size** that keeps a *bounded* overall false-positive rate without knowing the capacity up front. It maintains a **list of ordinary Bloom layers**; when the active layer fills to its capacity it is frozen and a **new layer** is appended — **larger** (capacity ×`growth`) and with a **tighter** target error (×`ratio`, `ratio < 1`). Because the per-layer error rates `P_i = P_target·(1 − ratio)·ratio^i` form a geometric series, their sum telescopes to `P_target`, so the compounded false-positive probability stays bounded for **any** number of elements (measured **0.0024 ≤ 0.01** after growth to 4 layers, and **0.0081 ≤ 0.02** at 40× the initial capacity). `contains` is a logical OR across layers (still **no false negatives**). This is the **dynamically-growing, capacity-free** membership filter — distinct from the platform's fixed-capacity Bloom (P72), deletion-supporting Counting Bloom (P107) and forgetting Stable Bloom (P110). Each layer is sized by the standard Bloom formulae; bits live in a `bytearray` and hashing is double-hashing from a seeded BLAKE2b digest salted by the layer index. Fully deterministic given the seed. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/scalable_bloom_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 118A: `pradyos/core/scalable_bloom.py` — `ScalableBloomError(detail)`; `ScalableBloomFilter(initial_capacity=1000, error_rate=0.01, ratio=0.9, growth=2, seed=0)` with `add(element)` → bool (False if already present; appends a tighter/larger layer when the active one is full), `contains(element)` / `__contains__`, `false_positive_rate()` (compounded `1 − Π(1 − P_i)`), `reset(...)`, `__len__`, and `initial_capacity` / `error_rate` / `ratio` / `growth` / `seed` / `num_layers` / `count` properties, plus `stats()` (count / num_layers / initial_capacity / error_rate / ratio / growth / total_bits / false_positive_rate / seed). Invalid `initial_capacity` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `error_rate` (∉ (0,1)) / `ratio` (∉ (0,1)) / `growth` (< 2) / `seed` raise `ScalableBloomError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 118B: `pradyos/web/scalable_bloom_web.py` — `register_scalablebloom_routes(app, scalable_bloom=None)` (defaults to a fresh filter) mounts 4 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/scalablebloom/add` (body `{element}`; 422 on missing; `{added, count}`), `GET /api/v1/scalablebloom/contains` (`?element=`), `GET /api/v1/scalablebloom/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/scalablebloom/reset` (body `{initial_capacity?, error_rate?, ratio?, growth?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 118C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase118.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `scalable_bloom` param, and a single `register_scalablebloom_routes(app, scalable_bloom)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 118D: `tests/test_scalable_bloom.py` (31) + `tests/test_scalablebloom_web.py` (18) — **growth** (≥ 3 layers past initial capacity; `total_bits` grows; low load stays at 1 layer); **no false negatives** after growth; **bounded FP** (≤ 0.015 near a 0.01 target after growth; ≤ 0.03 at 40× capacity; design bound ≤ target; tighter ratio still bounded); duplicate `add` → False + distinct `count`; **determinism** (same seed → identical layers & bits; different seed diverges); config validation (`initial_capacity`/`error_rate`/`ratio`/`growth`/`seed`, bools) + `ScalableBloomError.detail`; properties / stats; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent adds; all 4 endpoints over HTTP incl. growth-over-HTTP + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `hyperminhash`).

**Phase 119 — Complete.** All 255 test modules green. Sovereign Rendezvous Hashing / HRW (Thaler & Ravishankar, 1998 — *highest random weight hashing*) — a distributed key→node assignment scheme that, like the platform's Hash Ring (P73, consistent hashing), spreads keys uniformly and **minimises reassignment** when the node set changes, but by an entirely different mechanism: each key `k` is assigned to the node `n` **maximising a score** derived from `hash(k, n)`. No ring, no virtual nodes — just `O(N)` score evaluations per lookup. Two properties fall out for free and were verified empirically: **uniform load** (each of `N` nodes wins ≈ `1/N` of keys — measured 955–1047 per node over 8000 keys / 8 nodes), and **minimal disruption** — removing a node reassigns *only its own* keys (every other key provably unchanged) and adding a node pulls *only* the keys it newly wins (≈ `1/(N+1)`, measured 0.116 ≈ 1/9) to it, disturbing nothing else. Weighted nodes use `score = −weight/ln(h)` (a 3× node wins ≈ 3× keys — measured 2.98×); `get_replicas(key, k)` returns the `k` highest-scoring nodes for replica placement (first replica = `assign`). A different algorithm in the same distributed-hashing class as the Hash Ring — HRW scores vs ring positions. Deterministic given the seed. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/rendezvous_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 119A: `pradyos/core/rendezvous_hash.py` — `RendezvousError(detail)`; `RendezvousHash(nodes=None, seed=0)` with `add_node(node, weight=1.0)` (also re-weights), `remove_node(node)` → bool, `contains` / `__contains__`, `assign(key)` (argmax score; `RendezvousError` if no nodes), `get_replicas(key, k)` (top-`k` nodes; `RendezvousError` on `k < 1` or no nodes), `weight_of(node)`, `reset(seed=None)`, `__len__`, and `seed` / `nodes` properties, plus `stats()` (num_nodes / nodes / total_weight / seed). The score `−weight/ln(h)` uses `h ∈ (0,1)` from a seeded BLAKE2b of `(seed, key, node)`; ties broken by stringified node id. Invalid `seed` or non-positive `weight` or non-iterable `nodes` raise `RendezvousError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 119B: `pradyos/web/rendezvous_web.py` — `register_rendezvous_routes(app, rendezvous=None)` (defaults to a fresh ring) mounts 6 (all-static) route-method combos: `POST /api/v1/rendezvous/nodes` (body `{node, weight?}`; 422 on missing / bad weight), `DELETE /api/v1/rendezvous/nodes` (body `{node}`), `GET /api/v1/rendezvous/assign` (`?key=`; **400 if no nodes**), `GET /api/v1/rendezvous/replicas` (`?key=&k=` `Query(ge=1)`; **400 if no nodes**), `GET /api/v1/rendezvous/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/rendezvous/reset` (body `{seed?}`).
- ✅ 119C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase119.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `rendezvous` param, and a single `register_rendezvous_routes(app, rendezvous)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 119D: `tests/test_rendezvous_hash.py` (36) + `tests/test_rendezvous_web.py` (21) — **deterministic** assignment (member node, stable, insertion-order independent, different seed diverges); **uniform load** (within 15 %); **minimal disruption** (remove moves exactly the removed node's keys & nothing else; add moves keys only to the new node, ≈ 1/(N+1)); **weighted load** (3× node ≈ 3× keys; re-weight); **replicas** (distinct, first = assign, capped at node count, `k < 1` raises, empty raises); node management (add / remove present-absent / contains / numeric ids); validation (`seed`/`weight`/non-iterable nodes, bools) + `weight_of` absent + `RendezvousError.detail`; properties (`nodes` sorted) / stats; reset; concurrent assigns + mutations; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. assign/replicas **400** with no nodes + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `scalablebloom`).
- ✅ 119E: `scripts/prove.py` — 255 test modules registered (Phase 119 appends `test_rendezvous_hash.py` + `test_rendezvous_web.py`).

**Phase 120 — Complete.** All 257 test modules green. Sovereign Maglev Hashing (Eisenbud, Cilingiroglu et al., 2016 — *Maglev: A Fast and Reliable Software Network Load Balancer*) — Google's **consistent hashing** scheme and the **third** distributed key→node assignment algorithm, alongside the Hash Ring (P73, ring) and Rendezvous/HRW (P119, per-key argmax). Maglev precomputes a fixed-size **lookup table** of `M` entries (`M` prime, `M ≫ N`): each node proposes a pseudo-random **permutation** of the slots (`offset = h1(node) mod M`, `skip = h2(node) mod (M−1) + 1`, so `permutation[j] = (offset + j·skip) mod M` visits every slot since `M` is prime), and the nodes take turns claiming their next-preferred still-empty slot until the table is full. A lookup is then an `O(1)` index `table[hash(key) mod M]`. This yields **near-perfect even load** (measured `load_ratio = 1.01`, max/min slots — far tighter than ring hashing) and **small disruption** on membership change (measured ~0.12 of keys move when 1 of 10 nodes is removed, with no key mapping to the removed node), with the fastest lookups of the three. A *different* mechanism again — permutation-filled lookup table vs ring positions vs per-key argmax. The requested `table_size` is bumped to the next prime; the table is rebuilt on node changes; hashes are seeded BLAKE2b so it is deterministic. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/maglev_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 120A: `pradyos/core/maglev.py` — `MaglevError(detail)`; `MaglevHash(nodes=None, table_size=65537, seed=0)` (table size rounded up to a prime via `_next_prime`) with `add_node(node)` / `remove_node(node)` → bool (rebuild the table), `lookup(key)` / `assign(key)` (`MaglevError` if no nodes), `contains` / `__contains__`, `reset(table_size=None, seed=None)`, `load_distribution()`, `__len__`, and `table_size` / `seed` / `nodes` properties, plus `stats()` (num_nodes / table_size / nodes / min_load / max_load / load_ratio / seed). Invalid `table_size` (< 2) / `seed`, non-iterable `nodes`, or more nodes than table slots raise `MaglevError` (bools rejected); duplicate nodes deduped.
- ✅ 120B: `pradyos/web/maglev_web.py` — `register_maglev_routes(app, maglev=None)` (defaults to a fresh table) mounts 5 (all-static) route-method combos: `POST /api/v1/maglev/nodes` (body `{node}`; 422 on missing, **400** on table overflow), `DELETE /api/v1/maglev/nodes` (body `{node}`), `GET /api/v1/maglev/lookup` (`?key=`; **400 if no nodes**), `GET /api/v1/maglev/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/maglev/reset` (body `{table_size?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 120C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase120.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `maglev` param, and a single `register_maglev_routes(app, maglev)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 120D: `tests/test_maglev.py` (37) + `tests/test_maglev_web.py` (19) — prime helpers (`_is_prime` / `_next_prime`); table-size bumped to prime; **deterministic** lookup (member, stable, order-independent, different seed diverges); **even load** (`load_ratio < 1.10`; distribution sums to table size; all nodes present); **disruption** (< 0.20 of keys move on remove; no key → removed node); single node owns all; node management (add rebuilds / dup → False / remove present-absent / numeric ids); validation (more nodes than slots, `table_size`, `seed`, non-iterable, bools) + `MaglevError.detail`; properties / stats (incl. empty); reset; concurrent lookups + mutations; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. lookup **400** with no nodes + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `rendezvous`).
- ✅ 120E: `scripts/prove.py` — 257 test modules registered (Phase 120 appends `test_maglev.py` + `test_maglev_web.py`).

**Phase 121 — Complete.** All 259 test modules green. Sovereign Invertible Bloom Lookup Table (Goodrich & Mitzenmacher, 2011) — a probabilistic **key→value store that can be fully enumerated and differenced**, a capability the platform's filters and sketches lacked. The cells are **partitioned** into `k` sub-tables (one cell per sub-table per key, so a key touches `k` distinct cells); each cell holds four XOR accumulators — `count`, `key_sum`, `value_sum`, `key_hash_sum`. `insert` / `delete` XOR a key's `(key, value)` into its `k` cells and adjust counts by `±1` (a `delete` may drive counts negative — that powers reconciliation). Beyond a *best-effort* `get` (decodes a key only from a pure cell — measured recall 0.967 at load 0.15, **never a wrong value**), two operations make it invertible: **`list_entries()`** decodes the *whole* table by **peeling** — repeatedly find a pure cell (`|count| == 1` whose `key_hash_sum` matches the hash of its `key_sum`), emit its `(key, value)`, XOR it out of its other cells, exposing new pure cells — recovering **every** entry below the load threshold (verified 300/300; raises when overloaded); and **`subtract(other)`** combines two tables cellwise into an IBLT of the **symmetric difference**, which `decode_difference()` peels into *only-in-self* (positive count) and *only-in-other* (negative) — the basis of **set reconciliation** (verified: A\B and B\A recovered exactly). A *new capability* — listable, differenceable storage — distinct from the static Bloomier map (P114). Keys/values are any hashable (folded to 64-bit ids with a registry for output). Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/iblt_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 121A: `pradyos/core/iblt.py` — `IBLTError(detail)`; `InvertibleBloomLookupTable(num_cells=1000, num_hashes=4, seed=0)` (partitioned: `m = (num_cells // k)·k`) with `insert(key, value)` / `delete(key, value)`, `get(key, default=None)` (best-effort) / `contains` / `__contains__`, `list_entries()` (raises `IBLTError` if it cannot fully decode), `is_listable()`, `subtract(other)` → new IBLT, `decode_difference()` → `(only_self, only_other)`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `num_cells` / `num_hashes` / `seed` properties, plus `stats()` (size / num_cells / num_hashes / listable / seed). Invalid `num_cells` / `num_hashes` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `seed`, or an incompatible `other`, raise `IBLTError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 121B: `pradyos/web/iblt_web.py` — `register_iblt_routes(app, iblt=None)` (defaults to a fresh table) mounts 7 (all-static) route-method combos: `POST /api/v1/iblt/insert` (body `{key, value}`; 422 on missing), `DELETE /api/v1/iblt/delete` (body `{key, value}`; 422 on missing), `GET /api/v1/iblt/get` (`?key=`; `{key, found, value}`), `GET /api/v1/iblt/list` (`{entries, count}`; **400 if not decodable**), `POST /api/v1/iblt/reconcile` (body `{pairs: [[k,v],...]}` → `{only_here, only_other}`; 422 on bad pairs, **400 if the difference is too large**), `GET /api/v1/iblt/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/iblt/reset`.
- ✅ 121C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase121.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `iblt` param, and a single `register_iblt_routes(app, iblt)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 121D: `tests/test_iblt.py` (30) + `tests/test_iblt_web.py` (19) — **get** (never a wrong value; recall ≥ 0.95; exact at tiny load; contains; non-member absent); insert/delete/size; **list_entries** (full decode = inserts; empty; reflects deletes; raises + `is_listable` False when overloaded); **set reconciliation** (A\B & B\A exact; identical sets → empty diff; difference-too-large raises); arbitrary & integer key/value types; determinism; config validation (`num_cells`/`num_hashes`/`seed`, bools, incompatible/non-IBLT subtract) + `IBLTError.detail`; properties (partitioned `num_cells`) / stats; reset; 10-thread concurrent inserts (500 entries decode); all 7 endpoints over HTTP incl. the list **400**, reconcile set-difference + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `maglev`).
- ✅ 121E: `scripts/prove.py` — 259 test modules registered (Phase 121 appends `test_iblt.py` + `test_iblt_web.py`).
- ✅ 121F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 122 planned.

**Phase 122 — Complete.** All 261 test modules green. Sovereign b-bit MinHash (Li & König, 2010 — *b-bit minwise hashing*) — a **space-compressed similarity sketch**: where MinHash (P88) stores `k` full 64-bit minimum-hash values, b-bit MinHash keeps only the **lowest `b` bits** of each (often `b = 1` or `2`), shrinking the stored signature ~`b/64`× while preserving Jaccard accuracy via a **bias-corrected estimator**. Two sets of Jaccard `J` agree on a position with probability `J + (1 − J)·C`, where `C = 2^(−b)` is the chance two *different* minimums share their low `b` bits; the estimator inverts this: `Ĵ = (match_rate − C)/(1 − C)`. A larger `b` shrinks the correction (lower variance, toward full MinHash); a smaller `b` saves more space (measured: Jaccard within ~0.03 across overlap levels at `b=4, k=512`; mean error falls as `b` grows). This is a *different* algorithm from MinHash/P88 (full signatures) and MinHash-LSH/P115 (banded index) — the compact estimator you store or transmit at scale. The builder keeps full running minimums (needed to fold incrementally); `signature()` exposes the compact `b`-bit form and `jaccard()` / `estimate_jaccard()` compare two signatures. Universal hashing with seeded coefficients keeps it deterministic. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/bbit_minhash_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 122A: `pradyos/core/bbit_minhash.py` — `BBitMinHashError(detail)`; module-level `estimate_jaccard(sig_a, sig_b, b)`; `BBitMinHash(num_perm=128, b=2, seed=0)` with `add(item)` / `add_many(iter)`, `signature()` (compact `b`-bit tuple), `jaccard(other)` (bias-corrected; `BBitMinHashError` on incompatible / non-sketch), `signature_bits()` (`k·b`), `reset(num_perm=None, b=None, seed=None)`, `__len__`, and `num_perm` / `b` / `seed` / `count` properties, plus `stats()` (num_perm / b / count / signature_bits / seed). Invalid `num_perm` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `b` (∉ 1..32) / `seed` raise `BBitMinHashError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 122B: `pradyos/web/bbit_minhash_web.py` — `register_bbitminhash_routes(app, bbit_minhash=None)` (defaults to a fresh sketch) mounts 5 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/bbitminhash/add` (body `{element}`; 422 on missing), `POST /api/v1/bbitminhash/compare` (body `{tokens[]}` → `{jaccard}`; 422 on non-list), `GET /api/v1/bbitminhash/signature` (`{signature, signature_bits}`), `GET /api/v1/bbitminhash/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/bbitminhash/reset` (body `{num_perm?, b?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).

Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 123 — Complete.** All 263 test modules green. Sovereign Conservative-Update Count-Min Sketch / CU Sketch (Estan & Varghese, 2002) — a frequency sketch *strictly more accurate* than the platform's Count-Min (P76), differing only in the **update rule**. Both keep a `depth × width` counter grid and report `estimate = min` of an item's `depth` counters; but where Count-Min increments **all** `depth` counters, the conservative update computes `est = min` of those counters and raises each only to `max(counter, est + amount)` — i.e. only the counter(s) at the current minimum move. This provably **never under-counts** (the minimum still rises by the inserted mass) and **never exceeds the Count-Min estimate**, while sharply cutting over-estimation (measured against an inline reference Count-Min on a collision-heavy stream: **mean over-estimate 22.7 vs 44.3 — roughly half**; every key `CU ≤ CM`; heavy hitter exact within 2 %). The trade-off: conservative update can't be safely reversed, so it is an **insert-and-query** estimator with no `delete`. A *different* algorithm from Count-Min/P76 (all-counter increment) and Count-Sketch/P94 (signed + median) — same grid, smarter writes. Double-hashing from one seeded BLAKE2b digest; arbitrary-width Python int counters. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/cu_sketch_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 123A: `pradyos/core/cu_sketch.py` — `CUSketchError(detail)`; `CUSketch(width=2048, depth=4, seed=0)` with `add(item, amount=1)` (conservative update; `CUSketchError` on `amount ∉ ℤ⁺`), `estimate(item)` (min of `depth` counters), `reset(width=None, depth=None, seed=None)`, and `width` / `depth` / `seed` / `total` properties, plus `stats()` (width / depth / total / num_counters / seed). Invalid `width` / `depth` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `seed` raise `CUSketchError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 123B: `pradyos/web/cu_sketch_web.py` — `register_cusketch_routes(app, cu_sketch=None)` (defaults to a fresh sketch) mounts 4 (all-static) routes — **no remove (conservative update is irreversible)**: `POST /api/v1/cusketch/add` (body `{item, amount?}`; 422 on missing / bad amount), `GET /api/v1/cusketch/estimate` (`?item=`), `GET /api/v1/cusketch/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/cusketch/reset` (body `{width?, depth?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 123C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase123.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `cu_sketch` param, and a single `register_cusketch_routes(app, cu_sketch)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 123D: `tests/test_cu_sketch.py` (26) + `tests/test_cusketch_web.py` (17) — **never under-counts**; **`CU ≤ Count-Min`** for every key (vs an inline reference CM) + **CU mean error < CM**; exact at low load; heavy hitter within 2 %; `amount` increments (default 1) / `total`; determinism (same seed → identical counters; different seed diverges); validation (`width`/`depth`/`seed`, bools, `amount ∈ {0, −1, 2.5}`) + `CUSketchError.detail`; properties / stats; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent adds; all 4 endpoints over HTTP incl. never-undercount + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `bbitminhash`).

**Phase 124 — Complete.** All 265 test modules green. Sovereign Jump Consistent Hash (Lamping & Veach, 2014) — Google's strikingly compact consistent-hashing scheme and the **fourth** distributed key→bucket assignment algorithm, alongside the Hash Ring (P73), Rendezvous/HRW (P119) and Maglev (P120). Its whole state is a single integer — the **bucket count** — with no ring, score array, or lookup table. `assign` runs a short loop using the key's 64-bit hash as a seeded LCG: `b=-1, j=0; while j<num_buckets: b=j; key=key·2862933555777941757+1; j=⌊(b+1)·(2³¹/((key>>33)+1))⌋; return b` — `O(ln N)` time, `O(1)` space, zero allocation. It provably gives **uniform load** (measured 1937–2063 per bucket over 20k keys / 10 buckets) and **optimal minimal disruption**: growing `N → N+1` moves *exactly* `1/(N+1)` of keys, only into the new bucket (measured 0.0906 ≈ 1/11, every move into bucket 10, all others unchanged — the information-theoretic minimum). The trade-off vs ring/HRW/Maglev: buckets are an ordered range `[0, N)` with no arbitrary names, and only the *last* bucket removes cheaply. A *different* mechanism again — a stateless jump loop. The key folds via seeded BLAKE2b; the loop is deterministic. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/jump_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 124A: `pradyos/core/jump_hash.py` — module-level `jump_consistent_hash(key_hash, num_buckets)` (the Lamping–Veach core); `JumpHashError(detail)`; `JumpHash(num_buckets=1, seed=0)` with `assign(key)`, `assign_for(key, num_buckets)` (stateless probe), `set_buckets(n)` / `add_bucket()` / `remove_bucket()` (last only; raises on the final bucket), `reset(num_buckets=None, seed=None)`, `load_distribution(keys)`, and `num_buckets` / `seed` properties, plus `stats()` (num_buckets / seed). Invalid `num_buckets` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `seed` raise `JumpHashError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 124B: `pradyos/web/jump_web.py` — `register_jump_routes(app, jump_hash=None)` (defaults to a fresh hasher) mounts 4 (all-static) routes: `GET /api/v1/jump/assign` (`?key=`; `{key, bucket, num_buckets}`), `POST /api/v1/jump/buckets` (body `{num_buckets}`; 422 on missing / bad), `GET /api/v1/jump/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/jump/reset` (body `{num_buckets?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 124C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase124.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `jump_hash` param, and a single `register_jump_routes(app, jump_hash)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 124D: `tests/test_jump_hash.py` (30) + `tests/test_jump_web.py` (14) — **core** (in range, single bucket → 0, **monotone bucket-id growth as `N` grows**, invalid buckets raise); **assign** (deterministic, in range, numeric keys, `assign_for` matches & is stateless); **uniform load** (within 10 %); **minimal disruption** (moves only into the new bucket; fraction ≈ 1/(N+1)); **determinism** (same seed; different seed diverges); bucket management (add / remove / set / **cannot remove last**); validation (`num_buckets`/`seed`, bools, `assign_for` bad) + `JumpHashError.detail`; properties / stats; reset; concurrent assigns; all 4 endpoints over HTTP incl. minimal-disruption + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `cusketch`).

Sovereign Frugal Streaming quantile / Frugal-2U (Ma, Muthukrishnan & Sandler, 2014) — a quantile estimator in **O(1) memory** (essentially a single value), where the platform's other quantile sketches (GK/P91, KLL/P92, t-Digest/P79, DDSketch/P96, Q-Digest/P105, Moment/P106) all keep many summaries. For a target quantile `q` it holds an estimate `m̃` and an adaptive integer `step`; on each item it nudges `m̃` up (`x > m̃` and `rand() > 1 − q`) or down (`x < m̃` and `rand() > q`), with the step accelerating on consecutive same-direction moves and resetting on reversals — a stochastic-approximation chase that converges to the true `q`-quantile of a stationary stream and tracks a drifting one. Measured on a uniform[0,1000) stream of 200k (errors are *tiny* despite the constant memory): **median 498.4 (true 500), q=0.25 → 257, q=0.75 → 745, q=0.9 → 902**; estimates monotonic across `q`; it tracks a distribution shift (median 54 → 951) and lands a skewed (exponential) median at 79.7 (true ≈ 69). The *extreme-low-memory* point of the quantile design space — no buckets, no centroids, just a tracker. The coin is a seeded `random.Random` so a fixed seed + stream reproduce the run. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/frugal_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 125A: `pradyos/core/frugal.py` — `FrugalError(detail)`; `FrugalQuantile(quantile=0.5, seed=0)` with `add(value)` (Frugal-2U update; first sample seeds `m̃`), `add_many(iter)`, `estimate()`, `reset(quantile=None, seed=None)`, `__len__`, and `quantile` / `seed` / `count` properties, plus `stats()` (quantile / estimate / step / count / seed). Invalid `quantile` (∉ (0,1)) / `seed` / non-numeric `value` raise `FrugalError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 125B: `pradyos/web/frugal_web.py` — `register_frugal_routes(app, frugal=None)` (defaults to a fresh median estimator) mounts 4 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/frugal/add` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / non-number), `GET /api/v1/frugal/estimate` (`{estimate, quantile, count}`), `GET /api/v1/frugal/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/frugal/reset` (body `{quantile?, seed?}`; 422 on bad config).
- ✅ 125C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase125.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `frugal` param, and a single `register_frugal_routes(app, frugal)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Sovereign Cosine LSH / Random-Hyperplane LSH index (Charikar, 2002; Indyk & Motwani, 1998) — a **similarity-search index for cosine similarity over vectors**, the cosine counterpart to the platform's MinHash-LSH (P115, which indexes *Jaccard* over sets). Each item vector is reduced to a `k`-bit **SimHash** signature by `k` random hyperplanes (bit `i` = sign of the dot product with hyperplane `i`, drawn from a seeded standard normal); two vectors at angle `θ` agree on a bit with probability `1 − θ/π`, so the bit-agreement fraction estimates the angle and `cos(π·(1 − agreement))` estimates the cosine (measured within **0.04** of true across angles 0…π). The signature splits into `bands` bands of `rows` bits and buckets per band, so vectors collide in a band iff they match every bit — the tunable LSH S-curve, now over *angular* distance; `query(vector)` gathers band-bucket candidates and refines by estimated cosine ≥ threshold (measured **recall 1.0** on near-duplicate vectors; orthogonal correctly excluded at threshold). A *different* index from MinHash-LSH/P115 (min-hashes over sets) — random hyperplanes over real vectors — and the *indexed search* the SimHash estimator (P89) lacks. Deterministic given the seed. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/simhash_lsh_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 126A: `pradyos/core/simhash_lsh.py` — `SimHashLSHError(detail)`; `SimHashLSH(dim=64, bands=16, rows=4, seed=0)` (`k = bands·rows` hyperplanes of dimension `dim`) with `insert(item_id, vector)` (re-insert replaces; validates dimension + numeric), `query(vector, threshold=0.0)` → `[(id, cosine), ...]` desc, `similarity(a, b)` (estimated cosine), `remove(item_id)` → bool, `contains` / `__contains__`, `reset(dim=None, bands=None, rows=None, seed=None)`, `__len__`, and `dim` / `bands` / `rows` / `num_perm` (k) / `seed` properties, plus `stats()`. Invalid `dim` / `bands` / `rows` (∉ ℤ⁺) / `seed`, wrong-dimension or non-numeric vector, or `threshold ∉ [−1, 1]` raise `SimHashLSHError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 126B: `pradyos/web/simhash_lsh_web.py` — `register_simhashlsh_routes(app, simhash_lsh=None)` mounts 5 (all-static) routes: `POST /api/v1/simhashlsh/insert` (body `{id, vector[]}`; 422 on missing / non-list / wrong-dim), `POST /api/v1/simhashlsh/query` (body `{vector[], threshold?}`; 422 on bad), `DELETE /api/v1/simhashlsh/remove` (body `{id}`), `GET /api/v1/simhashlsh/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/simhashlsh/reset` (body `{dim?, bands?, rows?, seed?}`).
- ✅ 126C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase126.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `simhash_lsh` param, and a single `register_simhashlsh_routes(app, simhash_lsh)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 126D: `tests/test_simhash_lsh.py` (31) + `tests/test_simhashlsh_web.py` (18) — **cosine estimate** (self = 1, within 0.12 across angles, opposite ≈ −1); **retrieval** (near-parallel found, orthogonal excluded at threshold, sorted desc, threshold filters, **recall ≥ 0.9** on near-dups); **remove / re-insert / contains**; **determinism** (same seed → identical query; different seed diverges signature); validation (`dim`/`bands`/`rows`/`seed`, bools, wrong-dimension & non-numeric vectors, `threshold ∉ [−1,1]`) + `SimHashLSHError.detail`; properties / stats; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. wrong-dim 422 + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `frugal`).

**Phase 127 — Complete.** All 271 test modules green. Sovereign Random Projection / Johnson–Lindenstrauss sketch (Johnson & Lindenstrauss, 1984; Achlioptas, 2001) — a **distance-preserving dimensionality-reduction** sketch, a new capability for the platform. It multiplies each `d`-dimensional input vector by a fixed random `k × d` matrix (`k ≪ d`) of **Rademacher** entries `±1/√k` (each sign w.p. ½) to produce a `k`-dimensional sketch; since those entries are zero-mean / unit-variance after scaling, `E[‖Rx‖²] = ‖x‖²` and `E[⟨Rx, Ry⟩] = ⟨x, y⟩`, so the projection is an *unbiased isometry in expectation*. The Johnson–Lindenstrauss lemma then guarantees that for `k = O(ln n / ε²)` *all* pairwise **Euclidean distances and dot products are preserved within `(1 ± ε)`** with high probability — so similarity search, clustering and nearest-neighbour work on the small sketches at a fraction of the cost (measured: mean distance ratio **0.9992**, >85% of pairs within ±30% at `k=64`, distortion shrinks as `k` grows). Distinct from the platform's *hashing*-based sketches (MinHash/SimHash/LSH, which each preserve a single similarity): random projection preserves the *geometry* of the whole space — every distance and angle at once — in a dense real sketch. Exposes `project(vector)`, plus `distance` / `dot` / `norm` estimators on the projected space. Exposed at `/api/v1/randomprojection`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; the random matrix is drawn from a seeded `random.Random` for reproducibility. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/random_projection_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 127A: `pradyos/core/random_projection.py` — `RandomProjectionError(detail)`; `RandomProjection(input_dim=128, output_dim=16, seed=0)` with `project(vector)` → `k`-vector, `distance(a, b)` / `dot(a, b)` / `norm(v)` estimators over the projection, `reset(input_dim=None, output_dim=None, seed=None)` (redraws the matrix; optional reconfigure), `input_dim` / `output_dim` / `seed` properties, and `stats()` (`input_dim` / `output_dim` / `compression_ratio` = d/k / `seed`). Invalid `input_dim` / `output_dim` (∉ ℤ⁺) or `seed` (∉ ℤ), and wrong-dimension or non-numeric vectors, raise `RandomProjectionError` (bools rejected).
- ✅ 127B: `pradyos/web/random_projection_web.py` — `register_randomprojection_routes(app, random_projection=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/randomprojection/project` (body `{vector[]}`; 422 on missing / non-list / wrong-dim), `POST /api/v1/randomprojection/distance` (body `{a[], b[]}`), `POST /api/v1/randomprojection/dot` (body `{a[], b[]}`), `GET /api/v1/randomprojection/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/randomprojection/reset` (body `{input_dim?, output_dim?, seed?}`).
- ✅ 127C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase127.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `random_projection` param, and a single `register_randomprojection_routes(app, random_projection)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 127D: `tests/test_random_projection.py` (35) + `tests/test_randomprojection_web.py` (16) — **JL preservation** (distance / norm / dot ratios ≈ 1 in mean, >85% within ±30%, larger `k` lowers distortion); **algebraic identities** (linearity `R(a+b)=Ra+Rb`, scaling, zero→zero, `⟨Rv,Rv⟩=‖Rv‖²`, dot/distance symmetry, triangle inequality, basis-vector columns are exactly `±1/√k`); **determinism** (same seed → identical projection; different seed diverges); validation (`input_dim`/`output_dim`/`seed`, bools, wrong-dimension & non-numeric vectors) + `RandomProjectionError.detail`; properties / stats (incl. non-integer compression ratio); reset clears + reconfigures + same-seed reproduces; 10-thread concurrent projections; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. wrong-dim 422 + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `simhashlsh`).
- ✅ 127E: `scripts/prove.py` — 271 test modules registered (Phase 127 appends `test_random_projection.py` + `test_randomprojection_web.py`).
- ✅ 127F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 128 planned.

**Phase 128 — Complete.** All 273 test modules green. Sovereign Golomb-Coded Set (Putze, Sanders & Singler, 2007; Golomb–Rice coding, 1966) — a **compressed, space-optimal static set-membership** structure, a new capability for the platform. Where the Bloom family (P72/counting/scalable/stable/cuckoo/xor/binary-fuse/ribbon/quotient) keeps membership in a *live bit-array*, a GCS stores the set as a *compressed byte stream*: it hashes the `n` items into the universe `[0, N)` with `N = ⌈n/p⌉` for target false-positive rate `p`, sorts the fingerprints (dropping duplicates), and stores the **gaps** between consecutive fingerprints with **Golomb–Rice codes** whose parameter is the optimum `M ≈ ln2·(N/n) = ln2/p` for the (nearly geometric, mean `1/p`) gaps — each gap `g` written as `g // M` in unary then `g % M` in truncated binary. This reaches within ~1.5 bits of the `log₂(1/p)` information-theoretic lower bound per item — *more compact than a Bloom filter* (which needs `1.44·log₂(1/p)`): **measured 8.12 bits/item vs Bloom's 9.57 at `p=0.01`** (floor 6.64) — at the cost of being **immutable once built** and `O(n)`-decoded per query (the canonical use is shipping a compact set over the wire, à la Chrome's CRLSet). `contains(item)` re-hashes and walks the decoded gap stream with an early exit — **zero false negatives** and a **measured FP rate of 0.0093** against the 0.01 target. A *different* structure from every existing membership filter (those are mutable bit-array sketches; this is a static, near-entropy-optimal *compressed encoding*). Exposed at `/api/v1/gcs`. Pure stdlib (`hashlib.blake2b` fingerprints); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic given the seed. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/gcs_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 128A: `pradyos/core/golomb_coded_set.py` — `GolombCodedSetError(detail)`; `GolombCodedSet(items=None, p=0.01, seed=0)` (static — built from the full item set) with `build(items)` (rebuild, replacing contents), `contains(item)` / `__contains__`, `reset(p=None, seed=None)` (clear / reconfigure), `__len__` (distinct fingerprints), and `p` / `seed` / `num_items` / `universe` / `golomb_m` / `num_bits` properties + `bits_per_item()` + `stats()`. Internal `_BitWriter` / `_BitReader` (MSB-first, bounded to the exact real bit count so padding is never misdecoded) and a truncated-binary Golomb codec handling `M=1` (pure unary) through power-of-two (Rice) and arbitrary `M`. Items are type-tagged (`int 1` / `str "1"` / `bytes b"1"` never alias); invalid `p` (∉ (0,1)) / `seed` (∉ ℤ) / item type (float, bool, …) raise `GolombCodedSetError`.
- ✅ 128B: `pradyos/web/gcs_web.py` — `register_gcs_routes(app, gcs=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/gcs/build` (body `{items[], p?, seed?}`; 422 on missing / bad config / bad item), `POST /api/v1/gcs/contains` (body `{item}`), `POST /api/v1/gcs/contains_many` (body `{items[]}` → `{results[], count}`), `GET /api/v1/gcs/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/gcs/reset` (body `{p?, seed?}`).

Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 128D: `tests/test_golomb_coded_set.py` (48) + `tests/test_gcs_web.py` (21) — **membership guarantees** (all members present = zero false negatives; FP within 1.5×`p`); **Golomb codec** round-trips exactly across 11 `M` values incl. `M=1` & powers of two, consuming the bit stream exactly (no padding misread) + reader-exhaustion guard; **compression** beats Bloom `1.44·log₂(1/p)` yet stays above the entropy floor, smaller `p` ⇒ more bits/item, `universe = ⌈n/p⌉`, optimal `M`; **type handling** (str/bytes/int accepted & type-tagged; float/bool/non-iterable rejected); **fingerprint self-collisions only shrink the distinct count, never cause a false negative** (exact counts verified in a collision-free `p=1e-6` regime); validation (`p`/`seed`, bools) + `GolombCodedSetError.detail`; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent `contains`; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `randomprojection`).

**Phase 129 — Complete.** All 275 test modules green. Sovereign Flajolet–Martin / PCSA cardinality sketch (Flajolet & Martin, 1985 — *Probabilistic Counting with Stochastic Averaging*) — the **original distinct-count estimator** and the progenitor of every later cardinality sketch on the platform, with a fundamentally different mechanism: it estimates distinct counts from **bit patterns**. Each element is hashed; the **trailing-zero count** `ρ` of the (low) hash bits is geometric (`P(ρ=i) = 2^−(i+1)`), so setting bit `ρ` of a bitmap leaves a frontier whose **lowest unset bit** `R` satisfies `E[R] ≈ log₂(φ·n)` with `φ ≈ 0.77351`. **Stochastic averaging** routes each item to one of `m` bitmaps by a leading-hash prefix and averages the lowest-unset positions `A = (1/m)·Σ R_j`, giving estimate `n̂ = (m/φ)·2^A` with standard error `≈ 0.78/√m`. This is *different* from the platform's other cardinality sketches: HyperLogLog/P74 (harmonic mean of *max*-leading-zero registers), Theta/P93 (KMV min-hashes), Linear Counting (bit-array fill ratio), HyperMinHash/P117 — FM/PCSA is the bit-pattern-observable original they descend from. Mergeable (bitmap-wise OR). **Measured** (honest, `m=64`): mean estimate within ~**4%** of truth for `n ≳ m` (ratio ≈ 1.025 at n=5000, 1.037 at n=50000), typical single-run error ≈ **7.6%** (vs SE 9.75%), merge of two disjoint 5000-sets estimates 9817; the **empty sketch reports exactly 0** and — like the original FM — **very small cardinalities are overestimated** (the classic small-range bias, `n=1 → ≈1.29m`). Exposed at `/api/v1/fmsketch`. Pure stdlib (`hashlib.blake2b`); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic given the seed. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/fmsketch_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 129A: `pradyos/core/fm_sketch.py` — `FMSketchError(detail)`; `FMSketch(num_bitmaps=64, num_bits=32, seed=0)` with `add(item)` / `add_many(items)` → count, `estimate()` → float / `count()` → int / `__len__`, `merge(other)` (bitmap-OR; configs must match), `reset(num_bitmaps=None, num_bits=None, seed=None)`, and `num_bitmaps` / `num_bits` / `seed` / `standard_error` (`0.78/√m`) properties + `stats()`. `num_bitmaps` must be a power of two in `[1, 65536]`, `num_bits ∈ [1, 32]`, `seed ∈ ℤ`; items are type-tagged str/bytes/int (float/bool rejected) — all violations raise `FMSketchError`.
- ✅ 129B: `pradyos/web/fmsketch_web.py` — `register_fmsketch_routes(app, fm_sketch=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/fmsketch/add` (body `{item}`; 422 on missing / bad type), `POST /api/v1/fmsketch/add_many` (body `{items[]}` → `{added, estimate}`), `GET /api/v1/fmsketch/estimate` (`{estimate, count}`), `GET /api/v1/fmsketch/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/fmsketch/reset` (body `{num_bitmaps?, num_bits?, seed?}`).

Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 129D: `tests/test_fm_sketch.py` (39) + `tests/test_fmsketch_web.py` (19) — **accuracy** as multi-seed means (unbiased to ~8% at n=5000 & n=50000; larger `m` tightens typical error; loose single-run bound); **structural** (empty→0, count rounds, len, monotone, add-from-zero, **idempotent on duplicate adds**, add_many count, documented small-n overestimation); **determinism** (same seed identical; different seed diverges bitmaps); **merge** (≈ union of disjoint sets, OR-with-self idempotent, subset adds nothing, config/seed/non-sketch mismatches raise); validation (`num_bitmaps` power-of-two & ≤65536, `num_bits∈[1,32]`, `seed`, bools) + `FMSketchError.detail`; type handling (str/bytes/int; float/bool rejected); reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent adds; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `gcs`).

**Phase 130 — Complete.** All 277 test modules green. Sovereign AMS sketch / tug-of-war second-moment estimator (Alon, Matias & Szegedy, 1996 — the Gödel-Prize *frequency-moments* work) — a **streaming `F₂` (second-moment / squared-L2-norm / self-join-size) and inner-product estimator**, a new aggregate-estimation capability for the platform. Each update `(key, ±count)` is mapped by a sign hash `ε(key) ∈ {−1, +1}`; a single counter `X = Σ_i f_i·ε(i)` has `E[X²] = Σ_i f_i² = F₂` (the cross terms cancel because the signs are zero-mean and independent), so `X²` is an *unbiased* estimator of `F₂`. The classic **median-of-means** construction tames its variance (`Var[X²] ≤ 2F₂²`): average `X²` across `width` independent counters (relative SE `≈ √(2/width)`) and take the **median** across `depth` rows. With the same sign hashes, two sketches estimate the **inner product** `Σ_i f_i·g_i` (join size) via `median_r mean_c (Xᶠ·Xᵍ)`, and sketches are **mergeable** by counter-wise addition — the sketch is linear in the counts, so it natively supports the turnstile model (negative updates). **Measured** (honest, `width=64`, `depth=7`): mean `F₂` within ~**1.6%** of exact over 40 seeds, typical single-run error **6.4%** (median-of-means beats the per-row SE 0.177), `width=256 → 3.5%`; inner-product mean ratio 1.007, merge-linearity 0.998; **empty → exactly 0**, turnstile `+c` then `−c` cancels to 0, a single `−7` update gives `F₂ = 49`. This is *different* from CountSketch/P94 and Count-Min/P76, which answer *point queries* (per-key frequency): AMS estimates a *scalar aggregate* of the whole frequency vector — its second moment, L2 norm, or join size. Exposed at `/api/v1/ams`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic given the seed — the `width·depth` independent ±1 signs per key are sliced from the bits of a (multi-block) seeded `blake2b` digest. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/ams_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 130A: `pradyos/core/ams_sketch.py` — `AMSError(detail)`; `AMSSketch(width=64, depth=7, seed=0)` with `update(key, count=1)` (count may be negative — turnstile), `update_many(keys)` → count, `f2()` / `second_moment()` / `l2_norm()`, `inner_product(other)` and `merge(other)` (configs must match), `reset(width=None, depth=None, seed=None)`, and `width` / `depth` / `seed` / `num_counters` / `standard_error` (`√(2/width)`) properties + `stats()`. `width`/`depth` positive ints with `width·depth ≤ 65536`; `seed`/`count` ints; keys type-tagged str/bytes/int — violations (incl. bools, float keys/counts) raise `AMSError`.
- ✅ 130B: `pradyos/web/ams_web.py` — `register_ams_routes(app, ams=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/ams/update` (body `{key, count?}`; 422 on missing / bad type), `POST /api/v1/ams/update_many` (body `{keys[]}` → `{added, f2}`), `GET /api/v1/ams/f2` (`{f2, l2_norm}`), `GET /api/v1/ams/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/ams/reset` (body `{width?, depth?, seed?}`).
- ✅ 130C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase130.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `ams` param, and a single `register_ams_routes(app, ams)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 130D: `tests/test_ams_sketch.py` (43) + `tests/test_ams_web.py` (21) — **`F₂` accuracy** as multi-seed means (unbiased to ~8%; larger `width` tightens; loose single-run bound); **identities** (`l2_norm = √F₂`, `inner_product(self) = F₂`, `merge(self)` quadruples `F₂`, disjoint inner-product mean ≈ 0); **turnstile** (cancellation → 0, single `−7` → 49, default-count accumulation, `F₂ ≥ 0`); **merge** linearity vs exact summed-stream `F₂`; `update_many` matches per-item updates; **determinism** (same seed identical; different seed diverges counters); validation (`width`/`depth`/`width·depth≤65536`/`seed`/`count`, bools) + `AMSError.detail`; type handling (str/bytes/int; float/bool rejected); reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent updates; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `fmsketch`).
