**Phase 131 — Complete.** All 279 test modules green. Sovereign Priority Sampling (Duffield, Lund & Thorup, 2007) — a **bounded-size weighted sample that gives unbiased subset-sum estimates**, a new sampling capability distinct from the platform's Reservoir/P85 (uniform sample) and Weighted-Reservoir/P98 (a single weighted draw). Each arriving item `(key, weight>0)` gets a **priority** `q = weight / u` where `u ∼ Uniform(0,1]` (a deterministic per-key hash); the sketch keeps the `k` highest-priority items in a min-heap (lazy deletion on re-add). The threshold `τ` is the `(k+1)`-th largest priority — the largest priority among *evicted* items (`τ = 0` while ≤ `k` items have been seen, so the sample is then **exact**), and each retained item gets an **adjusted weight** `ŵ = max(weight, τ)`. Then for **any** subset `S`, `Σ_{i∈S∩sample} ŵ_i` is an *unbiased* estimator of `Σ_{i∈S} w_i` — so a single bounded sample answers arbitrary subset-sum / total-weight queries (addressed here by a **category** tag) with provably zero bias and variance `O(1/k)`. **Measured** (honest, `k=256`): mean total estimate within ~**1.4%** of exact over 40 seeds (ratio ≈ 0.986), typical single-run error **3.7%**, `k=1024 → 1.8%`; per-category sums unbiased (ratios 0.96–1.02); `N ≤ k` is **exact** with `τ=0`; the result is **order-independent** (identical total / sample / threshold across shuffles). This is *different* from uniform reservoir sampling (which estimates counts, not weighted sums) and from a single weighted draw: priority sampling is the unbiased-aggregate-over-a-bounded-sample primitive. Exposed at `/api/v1/prioritysample`. Pure stdlib (`heapq`, `hashlib.blake2b`); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic given the seed. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/priority_sampling_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 131A: `pradyos/core/priority_sampling.py` — `PrioritySampleError(detail)`; `PrioritySample(capacity=256, seed=0)` with `add(key, weight, category=None)` → sampled-bool, `add_many(items)` → count, `estimate(category=None)` (unbiased subset-sum) / `total()`, `sample_keys()`, `reset(capacity=None, seed=None)`, `__len__`, and `capacity` / `seed` / `num_seen` / `threshold` properties + `stats()`. Keys are type-tagged str/bytes/int; `capacity` positive int, `seed` int, `weight` a number > 0, `category` str-or-None — violations (incl. bools, float keys, zero/negative weights) raise `PrioritySampleError`.
- ✅ 131B: `pradyos/web/priority_sampling_web.py` — `register_prioritysample_routes(app, priority_sample=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/prioritysample/add` (body `{key, weight, category?}`; 422 on missing / bad), `POST /api/v1/prioritysample/add_many` (body `{items: [[key, weight(, category)], ...]}`), `GET /api/v1/prioritysample/estimate` (query `?category=`), `GET /api/v1/prioritysample/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/prioritysample/reset` (body `{capacity?, seed?}`).
- ✅ 131C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase131.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `priority_sample` param, and a single `register_prioritysample_routes(app, priority_sample)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 131D: `tests/test_priority_sampling.py` (41) + `tests/test_priority_sampling_web.py` (22) — **unbiasedness** as multi-seed means (total to ~6%, per-category to ~10%, larger `k` tightens, loose single-run bound); **exact when `N ≤ k`** (total & per-category exact, `τ=0`, holds all); **order independence** (total / sample / threshold identical across shuffles) & determinism; structural (capacity cap, `τ>0` when `N>k`, `num_seen`, sampled-bool, empty→0); `add_many` arity; re-add last-write-wins; validation (`capacity`/`seed`/`weight>0`/`category`, bools, float keys) + `PrioritySampleError.detail`; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent adds; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `ams`).

Sovereign Cuckoo Hash Table (Pagh & Rodler, 2001) — an **exact key→value dictionary with worst-case `O(1)` lookup**, a new capability for the platform. This is *categorically different* from the Cuckoo **Filter** of P86 (at `/api/v1/cuckoo`), which is an *approximate set-membership* sketch with a false-positive rate: a Cuckoo Hash *Table* stores the actual key/value pairs and answers `get` / `contains` with **zero error** in **at most two slot probes**, independent of load. Two tables `T1`, `T2` (each `m` slots) and two independent hashes give every key exactly two candidate homes; an item lives in one of them, so lookup checks both — *worst-case two probes*. Insert seats the item in its `T1` home and, if occupied, **evicts** the resident (re-seated in its `T2` home, displacing the next, …) — the "cuckoo" kicking chain; if the chain exceeds a bound the table **rehashes** (new seeds, growing if needed) and replays every item (amortised `O(1)`). The lookup cost is independent of item count or load factor — the defining cuckoo-hashing guarantee. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a Python `dict` found 0 mismatches over 20 000 mixed put/remove/query ops**; inserting 5 000 keys into a tiny `capacity=8` table grew it to 8 192 over 27 rehashes with **zero loss** and every key retrievable via the ≤2-probe path. Exposed at `/api/v1/cuckoohash` (distinct from the P86 filter at `/api/v1/cuckoo`). Pure stdlib (`hashlib.blake2b` for the two hashes); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic given the seed. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/cuckoohash_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 132A: `pradyos/core/cuckoo_hashtable.py` — `CuckooHashError(detail)`; `CuckooHashTable(capacity=16, seed=0)` with `put(key, value)` (insert/update), `put_many(items)` → count, `get(key, default=None)` (≤2 probes), `contains` / `__contains__`, `remove(key)` → bool, `keys()`, `reset(capacity=None, seed=None)`, `__len__`, and `capacity` / `seed` / `size` / `num_rehashes` / `load_factor` properties + `stats()`. Keys are type-tagged str/bytes/int (bool/float rejected → `CuckooHashError`); the kicking chain rehashes (new seed, then grows) on cycles, always replaying every item.
- ✅ 132B: `pradyos/web/cuckoohash_web.py` — `register_cuckoohash_routes(app, cuckoo_hashtable=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/cuckoohash/put` (body `{key, value}`; 422 on missing / bad key), `POST /api/v1/cuckoohash/get` (body `{key}` → `{key, found, value}`), `DELETE /api/v1/cuckoohash/remove` (body `{key}` → `{key, removed}`), `GET /api/v1/cuckoohash/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/cuckoohash/reset` (body `{capacity?, seed?}`).
- ✅ 132C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase132.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `cuckoo_hashtable` param, and a single `register_cuckoohash_routes(app, cuckoo_hashtable)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 132D: `tests/test_cuckoo_hashtable.py` (34) + `tests/test_cuckoohash_web.py` (24) — **exact-map semantics** (put/get/update/remove, len, keys, arbitrary value objects); **growth with no loss** across rehashes + the **two-probe invariant** (every stored item sits at one of its two homes); **a differential test against `dict`** over thousands of mixed ops; key types (int/bytes/str distinct & type-tagged, bool/float rejected); `put_many` arity; determinism; validation (`capacity`/`seed`, bools) + `CuckooHashError.detail`; reset clears + reconfigures; 10-thread concurrent puts; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `prioritysample`).

Sovereign Splay Tree (Sleator & Tarjan, 1985) — a **self-adjusting binary search tree** with amortised `O(log n)` operations and an *access-locality* guarantee, a new ordered-map mechanism for the platform. Distinct from the *randomised* balance of Treap/P113 and the *probabilistic levels* of Skip List/P78: a splay tree carries no balance metadata and instead **splays** every accessed node to the root via `zig` / `zig-zig` / `zig-zag` rotations (implemented here as the classic **top-down splay**), so recently/frequently accessed keys stay near the root and repeated-access and sequential workloads run faster than the `O(log n)` worst case (the *static-* and *dynamic-optimality* lineage). Supports ordered-map operations — `insert`, `find`, `delete`, `min`/`max`, predecessor/successor, in-order keys — each restructuring the tree by splaying. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a Python `dict` agreed on every `find`, the full key set, and size across 20 000 mixed insert/delete/find ops**; in-order traversal is sorted, `min`/`max`/predecessor/successor match a sorted reference, and `find`/`insert`/repeated-access provably leave the touched key at the root. Exposed at `/api/v1/splaytree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; **deterministic** — no randomness, so the tree shape is a pure function of the operation sequence. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/splay_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 133A: `pradyos/core/splay_tree.py` — `SplayTreeError(detail)`; `SplayTree()` with `insert(key, value=None)` (update in place), `find(key, default=None)` / `contains` / `__contains__`, `delete(key)` → bool, `min()` / `max()` (raise on empty), `predecessor(key)` / `successor(key)` → key-or-None, `keys()` (sorted), `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `root_key` / `key_kind` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Keys must be mutually orderable — `int`/`float` (one numeric kind) or `str` — bools and non-orderable types raise `SplayTreeError`, and mixing kinds raises; every access splays the touched node to the root via top-down splay.
- ✅ 133B: `pradyos/web/splay_tree_web.py` — `register_splaytree_routes(app, splay_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/splaytree/insert` (body `{key, value?}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind key), `POST /api/v1/splaytree/find` (body `{key}` → `{key, found, value, root_key}`), `DELETE /api/v1/splaytree/delete` (body `{key}` → `{key, deleted, size}`), `GET /api/v1/splaytree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/splaytree/reset`.
- ✅ 133C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase133.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `splay_tree` param, and a single `register_splaytree_routes(app, splay_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 134 — Complete.** All 285 test modules green. Sovereign Rank/Select succinct bitvector (Jacobson, 1989) — the **foundational succinct-data-structure primitive**: `O(1)` `rank` and `O(log n)` `select` over a static bit array using `o(n)` extra index bits, a new capability for the platform. `rank1(i)` counts the set bits in `bits[0..i)` and `select1(k)` returns the position of the `k`-th set bit (with `rank0`/`select0` duals); these are the operations every succinct structure (wavelet trees, succinct tries, balanced-parenthesis trees) is built on. Bits are packed into 64-bit words; a two-level index stores an absolute set-bit count before each **superblock** (8 words = 512 bits) and a relative count before each **block** (one word), so `rank1` is a superblock lookup + a block lookup + one partial-word `int.bit_count` — **constant time** — and `select` **binary-searches the cumulative rank** (`O(log n)`, cheap given `O(1)` rank). Distinct from the platform's *frequency/counting* sketches: this is an exact, deterministic index over a known bit array, not an approximate counter. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a naive scan matched `rank1`/`rank0`/`select1`/`select0`/`get` on genuinely-mixed bitvectors across 12 sizes — including word boundaries (63/64/65/127/128/512/513) and a superblock-crossing 6 000-bit vector** — and all identities hold (`rank1(i)+rank0(i)=i`, `arr[select1(k)]=1`, `rank1(select1(k))=k−1`). Exposed at `/api/v1/rankselect`. Pure stdlib (`int.bit_count`, Python ≥ 3.10); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static — built once from the bit array). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/rank_select_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 134A: `pradyos/core/rank_select.py` — `RankSelectError(detail)`; `RankSelect(bits=None)` (a `'0'/'1'` string or an iterable of `0/1`/bool) with `build(bits)` (static rebuild), `rank1(i)` / `rank0(i)` (`i ∈ [0, n]`), `select1(k)` / `select0(k)` (1-indexed; raise outside `[1, count]`), `get(i)`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `count1` / `count0` properties + `stats()`. Out-of-range indices/ranks and malformed bits (non-`0/1`, non-iterable) raise `RankSelectError` (bool indices rejected).
- ✅ 134B: `pradyos/web/rank_select_web.py` — `register_rankselect_routes(app, rank_select=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/rankselect/build` (body `{bits}`; 422 on missing / malformed), `GET /api/v1/rankselect/rank` (query `?i=&bit=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/rankselect/select` (query `?k=&bit=`, `Query(ge=1)`), `GET /api/v1/rankselect/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/rankselect/reset`.
- ✅ 134C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase134.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `rank_select` param, and a single `register_rankselect_routes(app, rank_select)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 134D: `tests/test_rank_select.py` (37) + `tests/test_rankselect_web.py` (23) — **a differential test against naive** for `rank1`/`rank0`/`select1`/`select0`/`get` over mixed vectors across 12 sizes + a superblock-crossing sparse vector; **identities** (`rank1+rank0=i`, `select`↔`rank` round-trips); edge cases (all-zeros, all-ones, empty, single bit, word boundaries); input forms (string / list / bool); select & rank bound checks (raise outside range, `Query(ge=…)` 422s); validation + `RankSelectError.detail`; build replaces; reset; 10-thread concurrent read queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `splaytree`).

**Phase 135 — Complete.** All 287 test modules green. Sovereign Wavelet Tree (Grossi, Gupta & Vitter, 2003) — a **succinct index over an arbitrary-alphabet sequence** that lifts rank/select from bits to symbols, built directly on the Rank/Select primitive of P134. Distinct symbols are mapped to contiguous ids `[0, σ)` in sorted order; the root stores one `RankSelect` bitvector marking, per position, whether its id lies in the lower or upper half of the alphabet range, and positions recurse into a left child (lower half) and a right child (upper half), `⌈log₂ σ⌉` levels deep. With `rank`/`select` on each level it answers, in `O(log σ)`: `access(i)` (the symbol at `i`), `rank(symbol, i)` (occurrences in `[0, i)`), `select(symbol, k)` (position of the `k`-th `symbol`), `quantile(i, j, k)` (the `k`-th smallest symbol in `[i, j)`), and `range_count(i, j, lo, hi)`. This is the symbol-generalisation of P134's bit rank/select and the backbone of compressed text indexes — *exact*, distinct from the frequency *sketches*. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against naive list operations matched all five queries** — `access`/`rank`/`select`/`quantile`/`range_count` — across 8 configs (σ = 1, 2, 3, 5, 7, 50, a string alphabet, and a wide/negative integer alphabet), with the identities `access(select(s,k))=s` and `rank(s, select(s,k))=k−1` holding throughout. Exposed at `/api/v1/wavelet`. Pure stdlib (reusing `RankSelect`); thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static — built once from the sequence). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/wavelet_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 135A: `pradyos/core/wavelet_tree.py` — `WaveletTreeError(detail)`; `WaveletTree(sequence=None)` with `build(sequence)`, `access(i)`, `rank(symbol, i)`, `select(symbol, k)`, `quantile(i, j, k)`, `range_count(i, j, lo, hi)`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `alphabet_size` / `symbols` properties + `stats()`. Symbols must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values and mixed kinds raise `WaveletTreeError`, as do out-of-range indices/ranks. Each node's split bitvector is a P134 `RankSelect`.
- ✅ 135B: `pradyos/web/wavelet_tree_web.py` — `register_wavelet_routes(app, wavelet_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/wavelet/build` (body `{sequence[]}`; 422 on missing / mixed-kind), `GET /api/v1/wavelet/access` (query `?i=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `POST /api/v1/wavelet/rank` (body `{symbol, i}`), `POST /api/v1/wavelet/quantile` (body `{i, j, k}`), `GET /api/v1/wavelet/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/wavelet/reset` (`select` / `range_count` remain on the core class).
- ✅ 135C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase135.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `wavelet_tree` param, and a single `register_wavelet_routes(app, wavelet_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 135D: `tests/test_wavelet_tree.py` (34) + `tests/test_wavelet_web.py` (22) — **a differential test against naive** for all five queries across 8 alphabet configs (incl. non-powers-of-two, strings, wide ints); identities (`select`↔`rank`↔`access`); edge cases (empty, σ=1, σ=2, single element); validation (mixed kind, bool, non-orderable, out-of-range indices/ranks, `select` overcount, absent symbol → rank 0) + `WaveletTreeError.detail`; `range_count` half-open / inverted / full-alphabet; determinism; build replaces; reset; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `rankselect`).
- ✅ 135E: `scripts/prove.py` — 287 test modules registered (Phase 135 appends `test_wavelet_tree.py` + `test_wavelet_web.py`).

**Phase 136 — Complete.** All 289 test modules green. Sovereign Skew Heap (Sleator & Tarjan, 1986) — a **self-adjusting meldable priority queue**, a new capability for the platform (no heap/priority-queue existed) and a thematic companion to the splay tree (both self-adjusting, no balance metadata). The single primitive is **meld**: keep the smaller of the two roots, meld its right subtree with the other heap, then **swap that root's children** — the swap is what amortises the right-spine to `O(log n)` with no rank/height bookkeeping. `insert` melds a singleton, `extract_min` melds the root's two children, and `meld` unions two heaps wholesale (the operation an array binary-heap lacks). This implementation melds **iteratively** — merging the two ascending right-spines into a sorted list and relinking from the back with the child-swap — so it is **immune to Python recursion limits on adversarial inputs**. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against `heapq` over 15 000 interleaved insert/extract ops** matched every `extract_min`; `meld` of two heaps equals the sorted union; and **20 000 ascending (and 20 000 descending) inserts complete with no `RecursionError`**. Exposed at `/api/v1/skewheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/skew_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 136A: `pradyos/core/skew_heap.py` — `SkewHeapError(detail)`; `SkewHeap()` with `insert(value)` (duplicates allowed), `extract_min()` / `peek_min()` / `find_min()` (raise on empty), `meld(other)` (unions; empties `other`), `keys_sorted()` (read-only), `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `kind` properties + `stats()`. Values must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values, mixed-kind inserts and mismatched-kind melds raise `SkewHeapError`. The meld is iterative (no recursion-depth risk).
- ✅ 136B: `pradyos/web/skew_heap_web.py` — `register_skewheap_routes(app, skew_heap=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/skewheap/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind), `POST /api/v1/skewheap/extract_min` (422 on empty), `GET /api/v1/skewheap/peek` (`min` null when empty), `GET /api/v1/skewheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/skewheap/reset` (`meld` stays on the core class).
- ✅ 136C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase136.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `skew_heap` param, and a single `register_skewheap_routes(app, skew_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 136D: `tests/test_skew_heap.py` (33) + `tests/test_skewheap_web.py` (19) — priority-queue semantics (extract in sorted order, peek, keys_sorted, duplicates, floats, strings); **a differential test against `heapq`** over 15 000 interleaved ops; **adversarial 20 000 ascending & descending inserts** (no recursion error); **meld** (= sorted union, empties other, into/with empty, self-noop, kind-mismatch & non-heap raise); empty-op & validation raises (bool, non-orderable, mixed kind) + `SkewHeapError.detail`; determinism; `kind` resets when emptied; reset; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `wavelet`).

**Phase 137 — Complete.** All 291 test modules green. Sovereign Interval Tree (Cormen–Leiserson–Rivest–Stein, augmented BST) — a **dynamic set of intervals supporting overlap and stabbing queries**, a new capability for the platform. Intervals `[low, high]` (endpoints inclusive) are stored in a BST keyed by `low`, and every node is augmented with `max` — the maximum `high` endpoint in its subtree — which lets a search prune whole subtrees: to find an overlapping interval, descend left when the left subtree's `max` reaches the query's `low`, else right. Supports `insert`, `remove`, `contains`, `overlap_any(low, high)`, `overlap(low, high)` (all intersecting intervals, with subtree-`max` pruning), `stab(point)`, and `count`. Every operation is **iterative** (the augmentation is recomputed along the recorded path), so the tree is immune to recursion limits even on adversarial sorted-`low` inserts. This is *different* from the platform's point-keyed ordered maps (Splay/P133, Treap/P113, Skip List/P78): it answers *range-intersection* queries via the subtree-`max` augmentation. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute-force scan matched `overlap`/`stab`/`overlap_any` over 300 queries**, the **subtree-`max` invariant held through 6 000 random insert/remove ops**, and **15 000 ascending inserts completed with no `RecursionError`** and a correct overlap query. Exposed at `/api/v1/intervaltree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/interval_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 137A: `pradyos/core/interval_tree.py` — `IntervalTreeError(detail)`; `IntervalTree()` with `insert(low, high)` (duplicates allowed), `remove(low, high)` → bool, `contains(low, high)`, `overlap_any(low, high)` → `(low,high)`|None, `overlap(low, high)` → sorted list, `stab(point)` → sorted list, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `max_endpoint` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Endpoints must be numbers with `low ≤ high` (bools and non-numerics raise `IntervalTreeError`). Insert/remove are iterative with bottom-up `max` fixup along the path; queries prune via subtree-`max`.
- ✅ 137B: `pradyos/web/interval_tree_web.py` — `register_intervaltree_routes(app, interval_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/intervaltree/insert` (body `{low, high}`; 422 on missing / `low>high` / non-numeric), `DELETE /api/v1/intervaltree/remove` (body `{low, high}` → `{removed, size}`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/overlap` (query `?low=&high=`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/stab` (query `?point=`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/intervaltree/reset` (`overlap_any` / `contains` stay on the core class).
- ✅ 137C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase137.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `interval_tree` param, and a single `register_intervaltree_routes(app, interval_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 137D: `tests/test_interval_tree.py` (33) + `tests/test_intervaltree_web.py` (23) — **a differential test against brute force** for `overlap`/`stab`/`overlap_any` + a 6 000-op random insert/remove sequence holding the **`max`-augmentation invariant**; **adversarial 15 000 sorted inserts** (no recursion error); inclusive-endpoint overlap, single-point & negative intervals, duplicates, `remove` (root / two-children / absent); validation (`low>high`, bool, non-numeric, non-numeric `stab`) + `IntervalTreeError.detail`; reset; `max_endpoint` / height / determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `skewheap`).

**Phase 138 — Complete.** All 293 test modules green. Sovereign Sparse Table (Bender & Farach-Colton) — a **static range-minimum/maximum index answering queries in `O(1)`** after `O(n log n)` preprocessing, a new capability for the platform. It precomputes `table[k][i] = aggregate of the 2ᵏ elements starting at i`, so any half-open range `[lo, hi)` is covered by **two overlapping power-of-two blocks** — `op(table[k][lo], table[k][hi−2ᵏ])` with `k = ⌊log₂(hi−lo)⌋` — a constant-time query, exact because `min`/`max` are **idempotent** (`op(x,x)=x`) so the overlap is harmless. This is *different* from the platform's *dynamic* Segment Tree (P81), which supports updates with `O(log n)` queries: a sparse table is **static** (built once, no updates) but answers in `O(1)`, the right tradeoff for immutable data. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against brute-force `min`/`max` matched every one of the `O(n²)` ranges for both ops across array sizes 1…100**, plus 2 000 random queries on a 5 000-element array. Exposed at `/api/v1/sparsetable`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static — built once from the array). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/sparse_table_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 138A: `pradyos/core/sparse_table.py` — `SparseTableError(detail)`; `SparseTable(values=None, op="min")` with `build(values, op=None)` (static rebuild), `query(lo, hi)` (half-open `[lo, hi)`, `O(1)`), `get(i)`, `reset(op=None)`, `__len__`, and `size` / `op` / `levels` properties + `stats()`. `op ∈ {min, max}`; values must be numbers (bools/non-numerics rejected); `query` needs `0 ≤ lo < hi ≤ n` and `get` needs `0 ≤ i < n` — all violations raise `SparseTableError` (non-int indices rejected). `k = (hi−lo).bit_length()−1` gives `⌊log₂⌋` in O(1).
- ✅ 138B: `pradyos/web/sparse_table_web.py` — `register_sparsetable_routes(app, sparse_table=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/sparsetable/build` (body `{values[], op?}`; 422 on missing / bad value / bad op), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/query` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0/1)`), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/get` (query `?i=`), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/sparsetable/reset`.
- ✅ 138C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase138.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `sparse_table` param, and a single `register_sparsetable_routes(app, sparse_table)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 138D: `tests/test_sparse_table.py` (33) + `tests/test_sparsetable_web.py` (21) — **a differential test against brute force** for every range (both `min` and `max`) across sizes 1…100 + 2 000 queries on a 5 000-element array; edges (single element, full range, adjacent, idempotent overlap, negatives, duplicates, floats); query/get bound checks (raise + `Query(ge=…)` 422s, non-int rejected); build validation (bad value, bad op, non-iterable) + `SparseTableError.detail`; build replaces & op change; reset; `op`/`levels` properties; determinism; 10-thread concurrent read queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `intervaltree`).

**Phase 139 — Complete.** All 295 test modules green. Sovereign KD-Tree (Bentley, 1975) — a **k-dimensional spatial index** for nearest-neighbour and orthogonal range search, the platform's first *spatial* structure. Points are stored in a binary tree that **cycles through the dimensions by depth** (axis = depth mod k) and is built by **median split** per axis (so it stays balanced, height `O(log n)`). `nearest(point)` descends toward the query, then **backtracks, pruning any subtree whose splitting plane is farther than the best squared distance found** (that branch cannot hold a closer point — comparisons use squared distance, no `sqrt`); `range(lo, hi)` reports all points inside the inclusive axis-aligned box, pruning a child when the box does not cross its splitting plane. This is *different* from the platform's one-dimensional ordered maps and interval tree — it answers *multidimensional proximity* queries. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `nearest` matched the brute-force minimum distance over 1 600 queries (k = 2 and 3, across many random point sets, compared by distance to allow ties)** and `range` matched a brute-force box scan; `k = 1` and `k = 4`, duplicates, single/empty all check out. Exposed at `/api/v1/kdtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static — built once, median-split per axis). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/kd_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 139A: `pradyos/core/kd_tree.py` — `KDTreeError(detail)`; `KDTree(points=None, dim=2)` with `build(points)` (static rebuild), `nearest(point)` → point|None, `nearest_dist(point)` → float|None, `range(lo, hi)` → sorted points, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `dim` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. `dim` a positive int; every point/query must have `dim` numeric coordinates; `range` needs `lo[i] ≤ hi[i]` — violations raise `KDTreeError`. NN backtracking prunes by `diff² < best²`; range prunes per axis.
- ✅ 139B: `pradyos/web/kd_tree_web.py` — `register_kdtree_routes(app, kd_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/kdtree/build` (body `{points[], dim?}`; 422 on missing / wrong-dim / non-numeric; may re-create at a new dimension via a shared state holder), `POST /api/v1/kdtree/nearest` (body `{point}` → `{nearest, distance}`), `POST /api/v1/kdtree/range` (body `{lo, hi}` → `{points, count}`), `GET /api/v1/kdtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/kdtree/reset`.
- ✅ 139C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase139.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `kd_tree` param, and a single `register_kdtree_routes(app, kd_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 139D: `tests/test_kd_tree.py` (32) + `tests/test_kdtree_web.py` (20) — **a differential test against brute force** for `nearest` (k=2,3; ~1 600 queries; by distance for ties) and `range` (k=2,3); `nearest_dist`; `k=1` / `k=4`; duplicates / single / empty / negative / float coords; degenerate box; validation (`dim`, wrong-dim, non-numeric, `lo>hi`, non-iterable) + `KDTreeError.detail`; build replaces; reset; balanced-height check; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 3-D build & 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `sparsetable`).

**Phase 140 — Complete.** All 297 test modules green. Sovereign Radix Tree / Patricia Trie (Morrison, 1968) — a **path-compressed prefix tree** for string keys, a new capability for the platform and a distinct, more compact cousin of the plain Trie (P83). Where a trie stores one character per edge, a radix tree **labels each edge with a whole substring** and collapses any chain of single-child nodes, so the node count is bounded by the number of distinguishing prefixes, not total key length — the structure behind IP routing tables and autocomplete. `insert` **splits** an edge when a key diverges partway along it; `delete` clears the key and **re-merges** a now-only-child node back into its parent; `prefix_search(prefix)` returns every key under a prefix; `longest_prefix(query)` returns the longest stored key that is a prefix of `query` (the routing-table lookup). This is *different* from P83's character-per-edge trie: edge compression makes it space-efficient and yields `longest_prefix` directly. The reported `compression_ratio` is the honest one — **characters stored per node** (a plain trie stores ~1). **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against `dict` matched `search` across a 15 000-op random insert/delete/search mix**, and `prefix_search` / `longest_prefix` matched brute-force scans; the prefix-of-another and delete-then-re-merge edge cases hold, and a shared-prefix set reports `compression_ratio ≈ 2.1`. Exposed at `/api/v1/radixtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/radix_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 140A: `pradyos/core/radix_tree.py` — `RadixTreeError(detail)`; `RadixTree(seed=0)` with `insert(key, value=None)`, `search(key)`, `contains` / `__contains__`, `delete(key)` → bool (with re-merge), `prefix_search(prefix)` → sorted `(key, value)` list, `longest_prefix(query)` → key|None, `keys()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `seed` properties + `num_nodes()` + `stats()` (`num_keys` / `num_nodes` / `compression_ratio` = chars-per-node). Non-string keys/prefixes (and non-int `seed`) raise `RadixTreeError`.
- ✅ 140B: `pradyos/web/radix_tree_web.py` — `register_radixtree_routes(app, radix_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/radixtree/insert` (body `{key, value?}`; 422 on missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/radixtree/search` (body `{key}` → `{found, value}`), `POST /api/v1/radixtree/prefix_search` (body `{prefix}` → `{results, count}`), `DELETE /api/v1/radixtree/delete` (body `{key}` → `{deleted, size}`), `GET /api/v1/radixtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/radixtree/reset` (`longest_prefix` / `contains` stay on the core class).
- ✅ 140C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase140.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `radix_tree` param, and a single `register_radixtree_routes(app, radix_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 140D: `tests/test_radix_tree.py` (35) + `tests/test_radix_tree_web.py` (22) — **a differential test against `dict`** for insert/search across 2 000 inserts and an 8 000-op insert/delete/search mix; `prefix_search` & `longest_prefix` vs brute force (incl. IP-routing-style); edge split, empty key, prefix-of-another, delete-with-re-merge / re-insert / delete-non-key-internal; `compression_ratio > 1`, `num_nodes`; validation (non-str key/prefix, bad seed) + `RadixTreeError.detail`; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `kdtree`).

**Phase 141 — Complete.** All 299 test modules green. Sovereign Suffix Array (Manber & Myers, 1990) — a **sorted index of all suffixes of a string** that answers substring queries by binary search, a new text-indexing capability that pairs with the Wavelet Tree (P135) and Radix Tree (P140). The array holds the starting positions of every suffix in lexicographic order; because all occurrences of a pattern share a common prefix, they form a **contiguous block** in that order, found by two binary searches (lower/upper bound) — so `contains`, `count`, and `positions` are `O(m log n)`. An accompanying **LCP** array records adjacencies, from which the number of **distinct substrings** falls out as `n(n+1)/2 − Σ LCP`. This is *different* from the platform's prefix trees — a suffix array indexes *every substring* of one text. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against brute-force scans matched `count`, `positions`, `contains`, the LCP array, and `distinct_substrings` across 37 texts** (incl. `banana`, `mississippi`, repeated chars, random); overlapping matches (`"aa"` in `"aaaa"` → 3), full-text and absent patterns, single-char and empty-text edges all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/suffixarray`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static — built once from the text). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/suffix_array_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 141A: `pradyos/core/suffix_array.py` — `SuffixArrayError(detail)`; `SuffixArray(text="")` with `build(text)` (static rebuild), `contains(pattern)`, `count(pattern)`, `positions(pattern)` (sorted), `suffix_array()`, `lcp_array()`, `distinct_substrings()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `text` properties + `stats()`. Non-string text/pattern and empty patterns raise `SuffixArrayError`; queries are two binary searches over the suffix array.
- ✅ 141B: `pradyos/web/suffix_array_web.py` — `register_suffixarray_routes(app, suffix_array=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/suffixarray/build` (body `{text}`; 422 on missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/suffixarray/search` (body `{pattern}` → `{contains, count, positions}`; 422 on empty/missing), `GET /api/v1/suffixarray/array` (`{suffix_array, lcp_array}`), `GET /api/v1/suffixarray/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/suffixarray/reset`.
- ✅ 141C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase141.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `suffix_array` param, and a single `register_suffixarray_routes(app, suffix_array)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 141D: `tests/test_suffix_array.py` (33) + `tests/test_suffix_array_web.py` (19) — **a differential test against brute force** for SA-is-sorted-permutation, `count`/`positions`/`contains`, LCP, and `distinct_substrings` across 37 texts; specific values (`banana` SA = `[5,3,1,0,4,2]`, distinct = 15), overlapping counts, single-char/repeated/unicode, pattern-longer-than-text, absent; validation (empty / non-str pattern, non-str text) + `SuffixArrayError.detail`; build replaces; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `radixtree`).
- ✅ 141E: `scripts/prove.py` — 299 test modules registered (Phase 141 appends `test_suffix_array.py` + `test_suffix_array_web.py`).
- ✅ 141F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 142 planned.

**Phase 142 — Complete.** All 301 test modules green. Sovereign Aho-Corasick (Aho & Corasick, 1975) — a **multi-pattern string-matching automaton** that finds *all* occurrences of *all* patterns in a text in a single `O(text + matches)` pass, a new capability for the platform. A trie of the patterns is augmented (by a BFS sweep) with **failure links** — on a mismatch the link jumps to the longest proper suffix that is still a trie node, so the text is never re-scanned (KMP generalised to a *set* of patterns) — and **output sets** that chain every pattern ending at a state via the failure path, so overlapping and nested matches are all reported. `add(pattern)` / `add_many`, `build()` (finalise links; also done lazily on first search), `search(text)` → sorted `(pattern, end_index)` matches, plus `count` / `contains_any`. This is *different* from the platform's single-string indexes (Suffix Array/P141, Radix Tree/P140): it matches a *dictionary* against a stream at once. **Verified** (honest): the **failure-link construction was differential-tested against a brute-force multi-find over 300 random pattern-sets**, and the textbook `{he, she, his, hers}` over `"ushers"` yields exactly `[(he,3),(she,3),(hers,5)]`; overlapping (`"aa"`×3 in `"aaaa"`), nested, suffix-via-failure-link, dedup, and auto-build-on-search all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/ahocorasick`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/aho_corasick_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 142A: `pradyos/core/aho_corasick.py` — `AhoCorasickError(detail)`; `AhoCorasick()` with `add(pattern)` → bool (dedup), `add_many(patterns)` → count, `build()`, `search(text)` → sorted `(pattern, end_index)` list, `count(text)`, `contains_any(text)`, `patterns()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `num_patterns` / `built` properties + `stats()`. Non-string / empty patterns and non-string text raise `AhoCorasickError`; the automaton auto-builds on the first search after a pattern is added (re-adding marks it dirty again).
- ✅ 142B: `pradyos/web/aho_corasick_web.py` — `register_ahocorasick_routes(app, aho_corasick=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/add` (body `{pattern}`; 422 on missing / empty / non-str), `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/add_many` (body `{patterns[]}`), `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/search` (body `{text}` → `{matches, count}`), `GET /api/v1/ahocorasick/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/ahocorasick/reset`.
- ✅ 142C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase142.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `aho_corasick` param, and a single `register_ahocorasick_routes(app, aho_corasick)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 142D: `tests/test_aho_corasick.py` (33) + `tests/test_aho_corasick_web.py` (20) — the classic `ushers` example, nested & substring-of-another patterns, unicode; **a differential test against brute force over 300 random pattern-sets**; overlapping count, `contains_any`, single-char patterns, suffix-match-via-failure-link; edges (no patterns, empty text, absent, pattern-longer); dedup + add/dup return values; auto-build / re-add-marks-dirty / explicit build; `add_many`; validation (non-str / empty pattern, non-str text, non-iterable) + `AhoCorasickError.detail`; reset; `patterns()` sorted; determinism; 10-thread concurrent search; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `suffixarray`).
- ✅ 142E: `scripts/prove.py` — 301 test modules registered (Phase 142 appends `test_aho_corasick.py` + `test_aho_corasick_web.py`).
- ✅ 142F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 143 planned.

**Phase 143 — Complete.** All 303 test modules green. Sovereign Binary (XOR) Trie — a **bitwise trie over fixed-width integers** that answers **maximum-XOR** queries greedily, a new capability for the platform. Each integer is stored as a root-to-leaf path of its bits from the most significant down (`width` levels, default 32); `max_xor(q)` walks the trie preferring, at every level, the child whose bit is *opposite* to `q`'s (maximising that XOR bit), so a single `O(width)` descent finds `max(q ^ x)` over all stored `x`. With per-node counts (a multiset) it also supports `min_xor`, `count_xor_less(q, k)` (stored values whose XOR with `q` is `< k` — the building block of XOR range queries), `insert`, `remove` (pruning emptied subtrees), and `contains`. This is *different* in mechanism from the character trie (P83) and radix tree (P140): a fixed-depth *binary* trie keyed on bit position — the structure behind max-XOR-pair and XOR-range problems. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test matched `max_xor` / `min_xor` / `count_xor_less` / `contains` against brute force over 1 800 queries (widths 4–32)** and an 8 000-op insert/remove multiset against a `Counter`; the classic max-XOR-pair (`max over x of max_xor(x)`) equals the brute-force best pair. Exposed at `/api/v1/xortrie`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/xor_trie_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 143A: `pradyos/core/xor_trie.py` — `XorTrieError(detail)`; `XorTrie(width=32)` with `insert(value)`, `remove(value)` → bool, `contains` / `__contains__`, `max_xor(query)` / `min_xor(query)` (raise on empty), `count_xor_less(query, k)`, `reset(width=None)`, `__len__`, and `size` / `width` properties + `stats()`. `width ∈ [1, 256]`; values/queries must be ints in `[0, 2^width)`; non-int `k` rejected — all raise `XorTrieError` (bools rejected). Per-node counts make it a multiset.
- ✅ 143B: `pradyos/web/xor_trie_web.py` — `register_xortrie_routes(app, xor_trie=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/xortrie/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / out-of-range), `DELETE /api/v1/xortrie/remove` (body `{value}` → `{removed, size}`), `POST /api/v1/xortrie/query` (body `{query}` → `{max_xor, min_xor}`; 422 on empty trie), `POST /api/v1/xortrie/count_xor_less` (body `{query, k}`), `GET /api/v1/xortrie/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/xortrie/reset` (`contains` stays on the core class).
- ✅ 143C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase143.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `xor_trie` param, and a single `register_xortrie_routes(app, xor_trie)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 143D: `tests/test_xor_trie.py` (33) + `tests/test_xor_trie_web.py` (22) — **differential vs brute force** for `max_xor`/`min_xor`/`count_xor_less`/`contains` across widths 4–32, an 8 000-op insert/remove multiset, and the **classic max-XOR-pair**; counted duplicates, `k` bounds, single value, empty raises; validation (`width`, out-of-range / negative / bool value, out-of-range query, non-int `k`) + `XorTrieError.detail`; reset / reconfigure width; `num_nodes`; determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `ahocorasick`).

**Phase 144 — Complete.** All 305 test modules green. Sovereign Min-Max Heap (Atkinson, Sack, Santoro & Strothotte, 1986) — a **double-ended priority queue** giving `O(1)` access to *both* the minimum and the maximum and `O(log n)` `extract_min` / `extract_max`, a new capability for the platform (the Skew Heap of P136 is a min-only meldable queue). It is a single array-backed binary heap whose levels **alternate**: a node on an even (min) level is `≤` all its descendants; on an odd (max) level it is `≥` all theirs. Insertion bubbles up against *grandparents* on the matching level type; `extract_min` / `extract_max` sift down by repeatedly swapping with the smallest/largest among a node's children *and grandchildren* (with a parent fix-up when a grandchild is chosen) — the level-parity logic that makes both ends cheap at once. Supports `push` / `push_many`, `peek_min` / `peek_max`, `extract_min` / `extract_max`, `keys_sorted`, `__len__`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `extract_min` yields ascending and `extract_max` descending order over 150 trials, an interleaved `extract_min`/`extract_max` mix matched a sorted deque over 100 trials, and the min-max invariant held through every push and extract**; level-boundary sizes 1–5, a 2 000-element drain, duplicates and strings all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/minmaxheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; sift-down iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/min_max_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 144A: `pradyos/core/min_max_heap.py` — `MinMaxHeapError(detail)`; `MinMaxHeap()` with `push(value)` / `push_many(values)` → count, `peek_min()` / `peek_max()` (raise on empty), `extract_min()` / `extract_max()` (raise on empty), `keys_sorted()`, `is_empty()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `kind` properties + `stats()`. Values must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values and mixed kinds raise `MinMaxHeapError`. Level parity is `(i+1).bit_length()−1 mod 2`; bubble-up compares grandparents; sift-down scans children+grandchildren.
- ✅ 144B: `pradyos/web/min_max_heap_web.py` — `register_minmaxheap_routes(app, min_max_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/push` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind), `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/extract_min` (422 on empty), `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/extract_max` (422 on empty), `GET /api/v1/minmaxheap/peek` (`min`/`max` null when empty), `GET /api/v1/minmaxheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/minmaxheap/reset`.
- ✅ 144C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase144.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `min_max_heap` param, and a single `register_minmaxheap_routes(app, min_max_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 144D: `tests/test_min_max_heap.py` (32) + `tests/test_min_max_heap_web.py` (20) — **differential vs sorted** for ascending/descending drains and **interleaved extract vs a sorted deque**, plus the **min-max invariant** through pushes and extracts; level-boundary sizes, 2 000-drain, duplicates, floats/negatives, strings; empty-op & validation raises (bool, non-orderable, mixed kind, non-iterable) + `MinMaxHeapError.detail`; `push_many`; `kind` resets when emptied; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent pushes; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `xortrie`).
- ✅ 144E: `scripts/prove.py` — 305 test modules registered (Phase 144 appends `test_min_max_heap.py` + `test_min_max_heap_web.py`).
- ✅ 144F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 145 planned.

**Phase 145 — Complete.** All 307 test modules green. Sovereign Cartesian Tree (Vuillemin, 1980) — a **binary tree built from a sequence** that is simultaneously a **binary-search tree on position** and a **min-heap on value**, a new capability for the platform. It is constructed in `O(n)` by a single left-to-right scan with a stack (each new element pops larger-valued nodes off the right spine, adopts the last popped as its left child, becomes the right child of whatever remains), and its in-order traversal recovers the original index order. Its defining property is the **range-minimum ↔ lowest-common-ancestor equivalence**: the minimum of any index range `[l, r]` is the value at the LCA of positions `l` and `r` (here via parent pointers + a depth array) — so `range_min` is an LCA lookup, with leftmost-on-ties. Supports `build`, `range_min(l, r)` / `range_argmin`, `inorder`, `sequence`, and exposes the `structure` (parent/left/right arrays). This is *different* from the doubling-table Sparse Table (P138): the same range-min query, via an explicit tree that also underlies treap construction and suffix-tree links. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `inorder == 0…n-1`, the BST+min-heap invariants, and `range_min` against a brute scan over *every* range across 120+ random sequences**; the root is the global argmin, ties take the leftmost, and a degenerate sorted 5 000-element input builds and queries with no recursion error. Exposed at `/api/v1/cartesiantree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/cartesian_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- ✅ 145A: `pradyos/core/cartesian_tree.py` — `CartesianTreeError(detail)`; `CartesianTree(values=None)` with `build(values)` (static rebuild), `range_min(lo, hi)` / `range_argmin(lo, hi)`, `inorder()`, `sequence()`, `structure()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `root_index` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Values must be numbers (bools/non-numerics rejected); `range_min` needs `0 ≤ lo ≤ hi < n` (non-int rejected) — all raise `CartesianTreeError`. Build is a stack; LCA is a parent-walk over a precomputed depth array.
- ✅ 145B: `pradyos/web/cartesian_tree_web.py` — `register_cartesiantree_routes(app, cartesian_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/cartesiantree/build` (body `{values[]}`; 422 on missing / non-numeric), `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/range_min` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0)` → `{min, argmin}`), `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/structure`, `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/cartesiantree/reset`.
- ✅ 145C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase145.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `cartesian_tree` param, and a single `register_cartesiantree_routes(app, cartesian_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- ✅ 145D: `tests/test_cartesian_tree.py` (33) + `tests/test_cartesian_tree_web.py` (17) — **differential vs brute** for `inorder`, BST+min-heap invariants, and `range_min`/`range_argmin` over every range across 120+ sequences; degenerate ascending/descending 5 000 (no recursion); leftmost-on-ties, root-is-global-argmin, single/empty, floats/negatives; validation (non-numeric, bool, `lo>hi`, out-of-range, non-int) + `CartesianTreeError.detail`; build replaces; reset; `structure`/`sequence`/height; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `minmaxheap`).
- ✅ 145E: `scripts/prove.py` — 307 test modules registered (Phase 145 appends `test_cartesian_tree.py` + `test_cartesian_tree_web.py`).
- ✅ 145F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 146 planned.

**Phase 146 — Planned.** Sovereign 2D Fenwick Tree (2D Binary Indexed Tree; Fenwick, 1994) — a **2-D point-update / rectangle-sum index** in `O(log²n)` per operation, a new capability for the platform (the Fenwick Tree of P80 is one-dimensional). Over an `R × C` grid it keeps, at each `(i, j)`, the sum of a rectangle of cells determined by the low-bits of `i` and `j`; `update(i, j, delta)` walks `i += i&-i`, `j += j&-j` and `prefix_sum(i, j)` walks them down — so the sum of any sub-rectangle is four prefix sums by inclusion-exclusion. Supports `update`, `point_value`, `prefix_sum(i, j)` (sum of `[0..i] × [0..j]`), and `range_sum(r1, c1, r2, c2)` (an arbitrary rectangle). This is *different* from the 1-D Fenwick (P80) and the range-min structures (Sparse Table/P138, Cartesian Tree/P145): it answers 2-D rectangle *sum* queries under point updates. To be exposed at `/api/v1/fenwick2d`; `fenwick2d` / `Fenwick2D` / `Fenwick2DError` / `register_fenwick2d_routes` / `/api/v1/fenwick2d` verified free on `origin/main` (all `[0]`). Pure stdlib; thread-safe via `threading.Lock`; deterministic.

> *Phase-map note:* the Phase 132 slot was pre-verified for **AnchorHash**, but its `K`/`W`/`L`/`R` removal bookkeeping could not be reproduced to the platform's zero-flaw bar with confidence, so it was **pivoted** to the Cuckoo Hash Table (a fully-verifiable exact structure, differential-tested against `dict`). AnchorHash remains available for a future phase.

---

## PradyOS v0.41.0 — Self-Driving

**99 test modules. 41 phases. Stdlib + asyncio only.**

A fully autonomous, self-driving OS kernel built in Python, with observe → alert → plan → react → heal → schedule → persist → remember → control-plane → heartbeat capabilities. The OS now drives itself — `HeartbeatLoop` ticks `ControlPlane` on a fixed cadence, which in turn ticks the scheduler, healer, and reactor in sequence. No external orchestrator needed.

The OS observes its own metrics (`SignalAggregator`), detects thresholds (`WatchpointSystem`), correlates signals (`CorrelationEngine`), records every decision into a cryptographically chained ledger (`DecisionJournal`), reacts to alerts via rules (`ReactorEngine`), self-heals degraded components (`HealingMonitor`), schedules its own work (`TaskScheduler`), persists state across restarts (`SnapshotStore` + `StateManager`), remembers context with TTLs (`MemoryStore`), wires it all together (`SovereignBus`), exposes a unified introspection layer (`ControlPlane`), and drives itself forward through an async loop (`HeartbeatLoop`).

**Phase 15 — Complete.** All 47 test modules green. Sovereign Scheduler — cron-style recurring campaigns with priority queues and SLA-aware routing:
- ✅ 15A: `pradyos/sovereign/scheduler.py` — `SovereignScheduler` class with
  injectable `clock` for deterministic testing. Pure-stdlib 5-field cron parser
  supporting `*`, `*/N`, and single-integer fields for minute/hour/dom/month/dow.
  `next_run_after(cron_expr, after_ts)` scans minute-by-minute in UTC.
  `add_job()` stores job dicts with `job_id`, `cron_expr`, `campaign_spec`,
  `priority`, `sla_seconds`, `next_run`, `enabled`. `remove_job()` / `enable_job()`
  / `disable_job()` return bool. `tick()` fires all enabled jobs whose
  `next_run <= clock()`, publishes `"scheduler.job.fired"` bus events, advances
  `next_run`, and returns the list of fired job_ids. `start()` / `stop()` manage a
  daemon background thread; both are idempotent. Thread-safe via `threading.Lock`.
- ✅ 15B: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` — five new endpoints wired via optional
  `scheduler` param in `create_app()`: `GET /api/v1/scheduler/jobs`,
  `POST /api/v1/scheduler/jobs`, `DELETE /api/v1/scheduler/jobs/{job_id}`,
  `POST /api/v1/scheduler/jobs/{job_id}/enable`,
  `POST /api/v1/scheduler/jobs/{job_id}/disable`. All return HTTP 200; safe
  empty responses when scheduler not injected.
- ✅ 15C: `tests/test_sovereign_scheduler.py` — 20 unit tests covering all
  scheduler methods, cron parsing, clock injection, bus event payload,
